Comprehensive Collection of Ancient and Modern Books: Volume 160

Throat Gate

Huangdi's Suwen

On Taiyin and Yangming

The throat governs the atmospheric qi, and the pharynx governs the earthly qi.
[Note: The throat is the gate of Taiyin's respiration, governing qi and belonging to heaven. The pharynx is the pathway of Yangming's essence, belonging to the stomach and governing the earth.]

Discussion on Yin and Yang

The combination of one yin and one yang is called throat obstruction.
[Note: One yin and one yang refer to Jueyin and Shaoyang. Jueyin wood governs qi and is transformed by the fire of Shaoyang; when wind and fire qi combine, the metal qi gets harmed, causing pain and obstruction in the throat.][1p]
Discussion on the Key Signs in Diagnosis

For those with the Yangming pattern, there is internal heat and dryness of the throat, frequent urination, and irritability. In severe cases, the tongue may curl up or the testicles may retract and end its function.
Annotation: The hand jueyin (pericardium) and foot jueyin (liver) are involved. The excess of wood and fire qi leads to internal heat and dryness of the throat, resulting in liver qi descending. Irritability indicates the elevation of pericardium qi. The liver is associated with tendons; tendons are concentrated in the genitals and connect to the root of the tongue, leading to symptoms such as a curling tongue and retraction of the sac.

Discussion on Coughing

In cases of heart coughing, coughing results in heart pain, and the throat feels obstructed like a block; in severe instances, there may be swelling of the throat and pharyngeal obstruction.
Annotation: The throat is an orifice of the lungs. The heart fire consumes metal, hence the throat feels obstructed. The hand shaoyin (heart) meridian starts in the heart and connects to the throat, leading to symptoms of swelling and pain in the throat.

Discussion on Wind

When someone suffers from wind in the spring, it is considered liver wind. Symptoms of liver wind include excessive sweating, sensitivity to wind, frequent sadness, a pale complexion, throat dryness, and irritability, with an occasional dislike for women; diagnosis may reveal a bluish hue below the eyes.
Annotation: The pulse of the foot jueyin circulates behind the throat and ascends to the jaw. When the wind from wood combines as a pathogen, it leads to excessive heat and dryness of the throat. Liver qi disorders cause irritability. Anger outweighs contemplation, resulting in occasional disdain for women. The eyes are associated with the liver, hence the examination reveals signs below the eyes.[2p]

Discourse on Counterflow

Counterflow of the hand-Yangming and hand-Shaoyang causes throat numbness, swelling of the throat, and difficulties in swallowing, which are ailments treated by the main physician. [Note: Hand-Yangming refers to the Lung's bowels, while hand-Shaoyang refers to the Sanjiao. Yangming governs the throat, the Lung governs the voice, and the fire energy of the Sanjiao is in counterflow, leading to throat numbness and swelling. Yangming is a channel of dryness and heat, while Sanjiao is associated with the heat of dragon and thunder; the combined heat in counterflow causes difficulties in swallowing.]

Explanation of Pulses

In the case of Jueyin, if there is severe throat dryness and internal heat, it is because Yin and Yang are deficient, leading to heat. [Note: "Severe" indicates excessive Yang energy. The energy of Jueyin is diminished by excessive Yang, thus also making Yin hot, resulting in severe dryness and internal heat.]

Major Discourse on the Six Fundamental Principles

Shao Yang governs the heavenly authority; the three energies lead to common illnesses of internal heat, such as deafness, blurred vision, blood overflow from sores, coughing and vomiting, nasal bleeding, thirst, yawning, throat numbness, red eyes, and a susceptibility to sudden death. [Note: The ailments of the people suffering from internal heat are due to the influence of wind and fire energy. The intersection of the two fires and the arrival of wind heat cause the susceptibility to sudden death.] The golden-tinged symptoms lead to coughing up counterflow, fullness in the chest and ribs radiating to the lower abdomen, leading to sharp pain that cannot be countered or turned; dryness in the throat, a dusty face, and a ghastly complexion. [Note: Counterflow of coughing and dryness are ailments of the Lung.][3p]
When the lesser yang arrives, it causes throat obstruction, tinnitus, and vomiting.

In the Year of the Great Yin, when dampness prevails, the people suffer from water retention, heart pain, deafness, and a swollen throat.

In the Year of the Lesser Yang, when dryness prevails, it may lead to a dry throat, dusty complexion, lack of bodily moisture, and external heat in the feet.

In the Year of the Greater Yang, when cold prevails, the people suffer from throat pain and swollen jaw.

When the Lesser Yang governs the heavens, and dryness prevails, the people suffer from a dry throat and dusty complexion.[4p]
Dry throat and dusty face are diseases of the liver meridian. When the sun governs, the cold prevails, causing people to suffer from a red face and yellow eyes, often accompanied by a dry throat.

(Note: The various symptoms arise from cold invading the heart fire, forcing it upwards, leading to a competition of water, fire, and heat.)

When the taiyin prevails, internal fire becomes stagnant, resulting in severe headaches and throat stiffness.

(Note: This is due to the mingling of wind and fire with dampness, ascending from the neck to the crown.)

When the yangming prevails, clarity emanates from within, causing throat obstruction. A great chill brings deathly stillness, leading to discomfort in the chest, throat obstruction, and coughing.

(Note: The cold and austere metal energy causes clarity to rise and results in throat obstruction and chest discomfort. Throat obstruction and coughing occur when the dryness of yangming metal rises to affect the lungs, creating mutual resonance.)

When the shaoyang governs, if external factors prevail, it leads to throat obstruction, headaches, throat swelling, and ear deafness.

(Note: All these are attributable to the invasion of damp heat causing illness.)[5p]
When the Yangming governs the heavens and the excess of clear and pure energy remains internally, there will be coughing, nosebleeds, and throat obstruction.

(Note: The excess of clear energy refers to the influx of pure and clean external energy into the body, resulting in a surplus. Coughing, nosebleeds, and throat obstruction are all ailments related to the lungs. The lungs are associated with metal and govern the heavens; therefore, the Yangming governing the heavenly energy may lead to illness in the lungs due to this internal excess.)

When the Taiyang governs the heavens and is dominant, there will be a sound in the throat.

(Note: This occurs due to the cold water energy below, which is expelled upwards from the lungs.)

One Yin and one Yang alternate and cease; this Yin energy reaches the heart, with no constancy in ascending or descending. The throat and esophagus become dry, resulting in illness in the earth and spleen.

(Note: One Yin refers to Jueyin, and one Yang refers to Shaoyang. If the energies of one Yin and one Yang alternate and cease, water cannot rise accordingly, leading to stagnant Yin energy that remains below the heart. The absence of constancy in ascending or descending indicates variability. The belly remains harmonized, and easy defecation indicates that water cannot adequately circulate through the limbs, causing difficulty in urination. If water cannot ascend and interact with the lungs, the throat and esophagus become dry. If it cannot nourish the central earth, then the earth becomes dry, leading to spleen sickness.)

From the "Spiritual Pivot Classic"

In the chapter on the manifestations of pathogenic energy affecting the organs,

The heart pulse is greatly disturbed, resulting in throat sounds.

(Note: The throat sounds refer to a resonant noise in the throat. The gathering of vital energy accumulates in the chest and arises to the throat, connecting the heart pulse to facilitate breathing. When heart energy is abundant, it produces sound in the throat.)[6p]
Meridian Section

The kidney's lesser yin meridian, when ill, presents symptoms of a hot mouth, dry tongue, swollen throat with difficulty in breathing, and dryness and pain in the throat. The triple warmer's lesser yang meridian, when moved, results in throat swelling and muscle lock. The small intestine's greater yang meridian, when moved, causes throat pain.

Note: These are ailments corresponding to the parts along the meridians.

Organ Section

When the lung is enlarged, it results in excessive thirst and is prone to chest tightness and throat obstruction with reversed qi.

Note: The lung is located in the chest, opening to the throat, and governs respiration; thus, when enlarged, it causes such ailments.

Worry and Anger Without Words Section

The throat is the passage for food and water. The larynx is the conduit for the upward and downward movement of qi. The epiglottis is the door to sound. The lips are like the fan of sound. The tongue is the instrument for sound. The uvula acts as a barrier for sound. The pharynx is where the control of qi is released. The horizontal bone governs the divine qi that directs the tongue's movement. If a person's nasal passages produce mucus and do not recover, the pharynx is obstructed, causing a loss of controlled qi. Hence, if the epiglottis is small and thin, it releases qi easily; its opening and closing are efficient, leading to a smooth outflow of qi. If the epiglottis is large and thick, its opening and closing are difficult, causing sluggish qi release and heavy speech. If a person suddenly loses their voice, it means cold qi has invaded the epiglottis, preventing it from producing sound; when sound cannot descend, complete closure and opening do not occur, therefore resulting in silence.[7p]
The upper passage of the stomach is the throat, which is responsible for the intake of food and drink; it lies behind the throat. The upper passage of the lungs is the throat, which governs the inhalation and exhalation of breath; it is located in front of the pharynx. The epiglottis is situated above the pharynx and is the junction of the throat; when a person eats or drinks, the epiglottis covers the throat, allowing the food to enter the pharynx. Thus, the throat's upper passage serves as the doorway for sound, from which vocal energy emanates. The mouth opens and closes to produce speech; hence it is called "shàn" (fan). The tongue must move to articulate speech, which is why it is referred to as "jī" (mechanism). The uvula is the soft palate between the throat, from which sounds emerge, thus referred to as "guān" (gate). The pharynx, known as "pángcè," is the upper opening of the palate, through which breath, mucus, and saliva communicate; hence it is called the place where breath divides, as breath is expelled from the mouth and nose through it. The horizontal bone at the base of the tongue is where spirit and energy circulate; therefore, it is the primary control for articulating the tongue. The nasal cavity expels mucus and saliva without retention; if the pharynx does not open, the division of breath is lost. The opening and closing of the epiglottis govern the emission of sound and breath; consequently, if it is thin, sound is produced rapidly, but if it is thick, opening and closing becomes difficult, and breath escapes slowly, hence speech becomes heavy. The proper energy of the Lesser Yin rises, and only then does the sound manifest; if cold energy lingers in the epiglottis, it cannot produce sound; thus it cannot open. If the sound cannot descend, it means it cannot close. Therefore, if opening and closing do not occur, there will be no sound produced.[8p]
Boils and Abscesses Section

Boils arise in the throat, known as "severe abscess." If severe abscess is not treated, it turns into pus; if the pus does not drain, it blocks the throat and can lead to death within half a day. For those that turn into pus and drain, it is advisable to consume pig fat and cold food, which is sufficient for three days.

Note: The throat is the gateway for breathing in and out; when it arises in the throat, its force is very fierce, hence the name "severe abscess." If the pus does not drain and blocks the throat, breathing becomes obstructed and death can occur even before half a day. The throat is the upper passageway of the lungs, and the lungs and kidneys are interconnected; pig fat and cold drinks help expel the heat toxin from below.[9p]
Jin Kui Yao Lue (Essentials from the Golden Coffer) by Zhang Ji from the Han Dynasty

Dryness

The disease of fox spirit resembles a cold. One feels a silent desire to sleep but cannot close the eyes, restless in both lying down and sitting up. It corrodes the throat as 'spirit,' and the lower body as 'fox.' There is no desire to eat or drink, and one finds the smell of food repulsive. The face may suddenly appear red, black, or white. If it affects the upper body, the voice becomes hoarse; for this, the prescription is Gan Cao Xie Xin Tang. If it affects the lower body, the throat feels dry, and Ku Shen Tang is used to wash it away.

For symptoms of weakness and internal urgency, palpitations, nosebleeds, abdominal pain, dreams of loss of essence, aching limbs, hands and feet feeling hot and bothered, dry throat, and dry mouth, Xiao Jian Zhong Tang is indicated.

For coughing that resists the direction, how can one discern that this is lung abscess? There will be pus and blood; if vomited, it causes death. What type of pulse is this? The master says: the pulse at the inch is weak and rapid. Weakness indicates wind, and rapidity indicates heat; weakness leads to sweating, while rapidity causes aversion to cold. Wind harms the protective layer, causing breathing issues; heat overburdens the nutritive layer, leading to difficulty in exhalation. Wind injures the skin and hair, while heat damages the blood vessels; wind housed in the lungs causes coughing.

The person has a dry mouth and labored breathing, a dry throat without thirst, excessive salivation with muddy foam, and frequently feels chills. The places passed through by heat cause blood to stagnate, leading to the accumulation of pus and abscesses, resulting in vomiting resembling rice porridge. If the condition is in the early stages, it can be treated; once pus forms, it leads to death.[10p]
Coughing with a feeling of fullness in the chest, quick pulse, dry throat without thirst, occasionally producing foul-smelling phlegm, and after a long time spitting pus like rice porridge indicates lung abscess, treated with Jie Geng Decoction.

If the patient suffers from watery swelling in the face, body, and limbs, with difficulty in urination, the pulse not indicating water but rather pain in the chest, the qi surging upwards into the throat, resembling roasted meat, with slight cough and shortness of breath. In accordance with the master's explanation, what kind of pulse is it? The master says: the pulse at the cun-kou is deep and tight. Deep indicates water, tight indicates cold. Deep and tight impinge upon each other, causing a blockage at the lower abdomen's gate. Initially slight, but heightened over time unnoticed. After yang declines, the nourishing and protecting energies interfere with each other. Yang damage leads to an excess of yin, causing cold to constrict slightly, kidneys' qi surging upwards, throat and pharynx becoming obstructed, and sudden sharp pain in the sides. If treated by retaining fluids and purging heavily, the qi fails to disperse, and the illness does not resolve. Later, heavy vomiting occurs, leaving the stomach weak and agitated, dry throat craving water, difficulty in urination, water and food undigested, and swelling in the face, hands, and feet. Moreover, administering Ting Li Pill to purge fluids, initially there may be slight relief, but excessive eating and drinking will cause swelling to return as before, with painful anguish in the chest and sides, resembling a wild dog. If water overflows, it leads to floating cough, panting, and counterflow of qi; one must first target the counterflow qi, allowing it to settle before treating the cough, as resolving the cough will subsequently alleviate the panting. First treat the new illness; the former illness will be addressed later.

Counterflow qi is ineffective.

Great counterflow qi surges upwards, with throat and esophagus having difficulty. To stop counterflow and promote downward qi, Mai Men Dong Decoction is prescribed.

When coughing with upward qi and a water hen sound in the throat, She Gan Ma Huang Decoction is prescribed.[11p]
Bi Pain

The disease caused by Yang toxicity presents as a red, spotted face like brocade, with throat pain and purulent blood in saliva. It can be treated within five days; after seven days, it is untreatable. The treatment is prescribed with Shengma Bieqiao Decoction.
The disease caused by Yin toxicity presents with a blue face, body pain as if beaten, and throat pain. It can also be treated within five days; after seven days, it is untreatable. The treatment is Shengma Bieqiao Decoction, removing arsenic and Sichuan pepper.

Pulse Criterion (Jin Dynasty, Wang Shuhe)

Dryness

When all three levels are floating, there is wind in the lungs, with copious nasal discharge and thick saliva. There is fever, aversion to cold, and pain in the flesh; the throat is dry, and the eyes weep with sour pain. The lung pulse is both floating and solid, the throat is dry and injured. Bowel movements are difficult and constipated, with the nose lacking fragrance. When solid and large, it is combined with slickness; the fur is burnt and the tears and saliva are sticky. Additionally, dryness in the throat is increased; in autumn, one should use acupressure in summer.

Throat Treatise (Tang Dynasty, Sun Simiao)

The throat corresponds to the spleen and stomach. It weighs twelve taels, is one foot two inches long, and two inches wide. Its circumference is twelve times, corresponding to the twelve hours. It governs the pathways of water and grains, facilitating spirit and qi. If there is internal heat, the throat will swell and block qi. Yujin ointment alleviates this. If there is cold in the organs, the throat will feel obstructed as if there is something stuck, with a constant urge to choke and a feeling of itchiness and phlegm. If there is heat, it should be opened; if cold, it should be unblocked. If it is neither hot nor cold, it should be adjusted according to the organs.[12p]
Complete Book of Sores and Ulcers
by Jin Dou Hanqing

General Discussion

Dou Menglin said: The throat is the crucial pathway for the essence of food and drink. The lung and large intestine are interconnected; the lung opens above to the throat, while the large intestine allows for the passage below. When food enters, life flourishes; when it ceases, life ends. Between life and death, changes in symptoms are diverse. Only the lung, governed by metal, regulates qi and generates bodily fluids, nourishing the entire body and moistening every bone. The cycle of life continues indefinitely, and when it flows smoothly, the five organs thrive and all passages are clear. However, if the dryness of metal is afflicted by the fire's invasion, it manifests swiftly, indicating a solar disorder. Thus, we treat by resolving heat and eliminating toxins, expelling wind and harmonizing qi, thereby restoring balance to metal. Danxi advised using rice vinegar to stir in the mouth to expel phlegm, which signifies alleviation. I believe excessive sourness causes dryness. First, use a bit of yellow ginger juice, add a little powdered Yuanming, and irrigate the throat to draw out phlegm; secondly, use vinegar water, adding more Yuanming powder to irrigate; finally, use honeyed water to moisten it. Gradually, phlegm can be expelled, thus opening the throat effectively. Additionally, using borneol powder for nourishment yields universally effective results.[13p]
If the wind obstructs the throat and the three initial medicines fail to expel phlegm, it is advisable to use raw tung oil to flush it, stirring with a goose feather, then use honeyed water to moisten it. Urgently take Niuhuang Qingxin Wan or Puo Tan Wan to descend the phlegm. Subsequently, take Erchen Decoction with adjustments; there is no case that does not heal. If the voice from the throat sounds like thunder, with anxiety from eating and swelling in the eyes, if the Tianzhu point is depressed, and the face is dark with lips scorched, the nose devoid of breath, eyes protruding, and sweating like beads, this indicates death. If it extends to the neck, the head and face become swollen, red like fire, and medicines cannot treat it, urgently use a magnetic needle to expel the bad blood. Use chicken egg white mixed with frankincense powder for immediate healing. Then use banana root juice to soothe the toxins. If the mouth and tongue are swollen and purplish-black, urgently prick to release blood. Blowing herbal powder afterward is highly effective, thus making this clear.

Breathing entails expelling yang and inhaling yin. During the intervals of breathing, the lungs govern it. Below the throat, if we speak of the six organs, it refers to the yin of the limbs; below the oropharynx, regarding the six bowels, it refers to the yang of the limbs. The organs are associated with yin as the internal, while the bowels are associated with yang as the external. Organs hide and store; they are where the spirits flow and circulate; bowels are repositories, governing the intake and distribution of food and essence. Below the throat, the six organs relate to the throat's response to the natural world; thus, they are connected to the lungs. Since lungs belong to metal and autumn represents heaven, and autumn's metal is thus, the path of natural phenomena allows for the unobstructed flow of breath.[14p]
The throat and the pharynx run parallel; they are actually two distinct parts, yet many people are confused about them. The throat serves as the air passage, while the pharynx is where food and water pass through, and the throat connects to the qi of the lungs below. It is said that the throat contains three orifices; this is incorrect. If the throat had three orifices, then food and qi would each pass through a separate orifice into the lungs, but since the lungs have no orifice below, how could they convey food and water to the lower energizers? The writings of the Yellow Emperor state: The lungs are the crown of the viscera, storing the true high qi within the lung meridian. Hence, clear yang emerges from the upper orifices, while turbid yin exits from the lower orifices. If people in the world do not know how to maintain themselves, the six qi of wind, cold, heat, dampness, dryness, and heat, along with the seven emotions of joy, anger, worry, thought, grief, fear, and shock, can lead to ailments as a result of mismanagement and overexertion, causing a hundred diseases to arise. Once diseases like sore throat, chronic cough, throat sores, and throat closure due to wind, toxins, or heat develop, one must seek their origin. When faced with these conditions—throat constriction, phlegm accumulation, or throat inflammation—appropriate measures should be taken, but one must not act indiscriminately; when there is a need to purge, one should do so appropriately, and should not treat rashly. Such conditions pertain to the very foundation of life and death; without recognizing their roots and branches, attacking them recklessly will lead to misfortune almost immediately. Danxi noted: The throat and pharynx are essential for the entire body, connecting with the stomach and serving as the exit of breath. If heat and toxins accumulate in the chest, they can generate wind phlegm, leading to stagnation and resulting in throat diseases.[15p]
Sores develop in the throat, sometimes resembling flesh, with red swelling causing obstruction and making it difficult to swallow, leading to severe cases where a heavy tongue emerges. The primary treatment first aims to eliminate wind and phlegm to clear the throat and diaphragm, then to resolve the heat and toxins, as delays may lead to irretrievable conditions. Additionally, heat and toxins may surge to the palate and cause sores, known as "suspended boils." Along with internal cold, this can also cause difficulty in swallowing and expectoration, hence a resolving method should be employed. Some say that treatment depends on the intensity of fire; if mild, treat directly; if severe, take countermeasures, inspect for phlegm and blood, and treat accordingly. Blood can be drawn at the lesser merchant point of the thumb to circulate qi. For those conditions that reach the exterior, external application of medication is essential. I have previously dipped a goose feather in rice vinegar to extract phlegm from the throat, as the acidity can help consolidate phlegm and disperse stagnant blood. If there are moths that do not disperse, use a small knife to draw blood just off the moth and apply powdered lead carbonate to the throat to dispel heat evils; take herbs such as changshan, indigo, licorice, platycodon, scutellaria, gardenia, rhubarb, and alum, adjusting the formula according to the symptoms to clear heat from the upper burner. Externally, herbs such as raw rehmannia, dragon liver, and leek roots can be used. If there are sores in the throat, whether white or red and often with bleeding, this is largely due to phlegm heat. First expel it with tung oil, then use licorice decoction to resolve the qi of the tung oil.[16p]
The affliction known as "choking wind" is associated with phlegm heat; when both the inner and outer throat are swollen, this is the condition. If there is no swelling externally, the body will be warm and the face red, indicating an extreme presence of heat and toxins. When there is swelling externally, the body is also warm, which is the result of the evils of fire manifesting outwardly. Sometimes the jaw is not strong, and there is no external swelling, but the throat is red, which indicates sudden sensitivity, and heat is present in the heart. If the affliction shifts from the left side to the right side, this is due to the lingering toxins not having left the body.

The throat can present various conditions: there may be accumulated heat, wind heat, pathogenic heat, or residual toxins after an illness, causing changes resembling a double-breasted moth. For example, if the throat is swollen and red for several days, shining like a mirror, this indicates accumulated heat. If the throat is swollen, slightly white, and shaped like an arm, this is due to wind toxin throat obstruction; this occurs when heat toxins encounter wind and fight against each other. If there is swelling in the throat with a purplish hue, this represents pathogenic heat, suggesting that the person is suffering from sudden exposure to heat toxins which congest the throat. It is essential to use herbs such as Mutong, Yuanshen, Shengdi, Huangqin, Huanglian, and Shanzhizi to clear the heart fire.

If one experiences shifting changes in the tongue, this indicates that heat has accumulated in the chest, hence the foul phlegm in the mouth. It is important to take cooling medications and apply treatments with borneol for support; one might also use a small (gold non-)knife to prick it to release purplish blood or toxins.

Why does throat obstruction cause swelling both internally and externally? This is due to the accumulation of wind and toxins in the throat, which results in congestion, stemming from a clash between wind toxins and phlegm. As stated in the "Suwen": without wind, phlegm does not move; without phlegm, one is not affected by wind.[17p]
When phlegm collides with wind, it blocks the throat. Externally, the throat appears about the size of an egg, slightly white in color, with swelling on the outside resembling sores. The body experiences chills and fever, the jaw is tightly clenched, and speech is not possible. First, use a mixture of water and pre-cooked flour or honey soup to extract the phlegm, and promptly take a decoction of Jingfang Disinfectant Powder. If there is swelling between the teeth that is purple-black, puncture it with a small knife and blow powdered borneol on it; this will be effective.

If the patient has a heavy tongue like a lotus flower, this indicates heat rising with wind, the fiery heart ascending. The treatment is the same as before.

If after recovery, the patient has a foul mouth and abdominal cramps, this is because heat toxins accumulate in the spleen; urgently use Suzi Jiangqi Decoction.

If after recovery, the patient has a dry, painful throat, this suggests the kidney's water is depleted, heart fire rushing upwards, consuming body fluids. First use ingredients like Ophiopogon, Schisandra, Ginseng, Apricot kernel, Asparagus, Licorice, Trillium, Rehmannia, Angelica, Platycodon, and Gardenia seeds, dissolve them in Shuangqing Pills.

If after recovery the patient experiences shortness of breath and cannot speak, it indicates the lung qi is obstructed; enhance Jiangqi Decoction with more Qianhu and add ginger juice at the time of administration. If the voice is hoarse or silent after illness, this signifies punishment of the lung meridian, and the outlook is grim.

If there is wind-heat closure of the throat, both internally and externally swollen, it means the person has long accumulated heat toxins and then contracted wind, resulting in wind and heat colliding and blocking the throat. This person also has a red face, swollen cheeks, experiences chills and fever, and has a lump in the throat the size of a fist, with fresh red blood externally.[18p]
First, use jade-character honey to adjust the treatment, then apply a modified Jingfang disinfectant decoction. If the jaw is tightly locked and cannot open, this is due to wind-phlegm clashing and obstructing the throat. First, use a wooden needle to clear the blockage; apply juice from yellow vegetable, warm honey soup, or vinegar water, all mixed with Yuanming powder to wash down the throat. Then stir with a goose feather to expel several bowls of phlegm, and externally apply a mixture of five parts powder and vinegar. Quickly take the Jingfang Erchen decoction, followed by blowing in Bingsu powder.

If there is an ulcer in the throat with a yellow hue, probe for phlegm as before. Use a small knife to pierce the ulcer to release pus, then blow in Bingsu powder and take a mouse sticky herb detoxifying decoction.

If the throat is closed due to wind-heat, this results from the patient accumulating heat toxins over a long period, leading to wind exposure and the clash of wind and heat, manifesting outwardly. The treatment method remains the same.

If it’s due to virtual yang rising, resulting from chronic illness with weakened vital energy, causing evil fire to ascend, the throat becomes swollen and painful. There is a lack of balance between water and fire, and heart fire surges towards the throat, leading to swelling and obstruction. The signs include inability to speak, tightly locked jaws, a mouth full of phlegm, cold hands and feet, and dizziness. The treatment method is as mentioned before.

If the condition is severe, the patient may be unresponsive with wide-open eyes and staring gaze; grind fructus corni and mix it with vinegar to apply to the soles of the feet, then use a decoction to lower Qi. If there is shortness of breath, add Qianhu and Wuyao; if there is breathlessness, add Chenxiang and Ginseng. Once the hands and feet become warm, drink thin porridge to restore vital energy. Entering the valley leads to prosperity; if one leaves the valley, it leads to demise. This is what it means.[19p]
If there is swelling around the jaw and red on the outside, this must be due to wind toxin. Urgently use紫苏 (perilla), maple leaves, and cypress branches to brew a soup and wash it. For external use, apply a potion of荆防 (aprl) and 羌活 (schizonepeta) to dispel the wind, or use 十宣散 (Ten Xuan Powder).

If the patient’s hands and feet are cold and the lips tremble, it is advisable to use小续命汤 (Small Revive Life Decoction), brewed with ginger and jujube, taken hot.

If the illness is localized to the right side, where residual toxins have not been removed, urgently take牛蒡子汤 (Burdock Seed Decoction) or a breath-reducing decoction with modifications for treatment.

If there is dryness in the mouth, night sweats causing insomnia, and occasional delirium with erratic movements, use十味人参散 (Ten Flavor Ginseng Powder) to treat it. The juice from地松 (pine) is also effective. Grind谷精草 (plantain) to a powder and blow it into the mouth; the juice from小青草 (small grass) is also beneficial. Mix雄黄 (realgar),元明粉 (calomel), and白矾 (alum) into a powder and blow it to induce expectoration.[20p]
In cases where one cannot sleep at night after an illness, with a lack of bodily fluids, treat with apricot-jujube paste or ginseng and sour jujube seed decoction.

In cases where the yang energy is weak and ascending, with no balance of water and fire, lower back cold without pain or itching, excessive phlegm in the mouth, and darkened lips, do not treat.

In cases where the mouth is red, there is bloody vomiting, and accompanied by phlegm and wheezing with a bluish face, do not treat.

In cases where the hands and feet are cold, the voice is inaudible, and there is a dry, painful throat without swelling, do not treat.

In cases where the hands and feet are cold and cannot retract, the neck is low and cannot rise, and there is dizziness with darkened vision, do not treat.

In cases where the tongue is rolled and cannot swallow, this is due to heat and toxicity rising; urgently use Zixue powder combined with musk to apply on the tongue, and then blow with Bingshi powder.

In cases of throat swelling and the reoccurrence of a heavy tongue, both of these channels are afflicted, indicating the presence of evil influences. Heart evil manifests under the tongue, and stomach evil emerges from the throat.[21p]
If there is a malignancy in the throat that arises from the heart meridian, then both ailments will manifest simultaneously, with external symptoms including headache, stiff neck, and feverish body. The method for examining phlegm is the same as before; additionally, use Zixue and Bingpian powder for treatment.

If there are over ten days of contracted cold with post-illness agitation, sore throat, a curled tongue, and a shrunken appearance, it is untreatable. If after more than ten days the illness remains unresolved with transmission leading to sore throat, and external symptoms like blue lips and curled tongue appear, this condition belongs to the uterine meridian and is difficult to treat. A dry sore throat with no phlegm is untreatable. Sore throat with a curled lip is untreatable. Sore throat with sweating in the head is untreatable. A black mouth indicates difficulty in treatment. Nasal congestion is untreatable.

If there is swelling in the throat and sores on the tongue, this indicates heat affecting the heart. Prolonged heat in the heart can lead to closure of the throat, and residual toxins drying the heart can result in tongue sores. One should use Bingpian powder and modify the Yuantan Shengma decoction for treatment. Its form resembles that of the bayberry, hence it is called "heavy palate." If there is closure of the throat due to alcohol poisoning, and the alcohol has impacted both the heart and spleen channels, leading to throat obstruction, the individual will have a flushed face and upward-looking eyes. The phlegm-extraction method remains the same, followed by the use of Bingpian powder for blowing and cooling drinks.

If suddenly there is swelling and enlargement in the mouth, it is known as "flying ulcer," which can be fatal. Use a small knife to puncture for bleeding, and add moss to detoxify, along with safflower and peony root. Difficulty with nausea and abdominal bloating is difficult to treat.

Generally, the treatment method is the same for men and women. However, if a woman has swelling in the throat that is red in color, this signifies menstrual irregularity.[22p]
If the meridians cannot function, it leads to blockages above, resulting in swelling and pain in the throat, attributed to disharmony between nourishment and defense. Men are primarily governed by qi, while women are primarily governed by blood. Each gender should adjust their treatment according to their specific qi and blood. It is advisable to use the Rong Decoction for this. If the condition is severe, with a pale complexion and cold feet, this indicates a deficiency of yang rising upwards; the appropriate treatment would be to take the Jiangqi Decoction, along with sputum-expectorant medicine as before. For pregnant women experiencing heart pain, do not treat. If the jaws are tightly locked and cannot open, with chest distress and a complete absence of qi, one may use ground soapberry to blow into the throat. If a woman experiences throat pain before childbirth and has a floating pulse, do not treat. If the face is red and the eyes are directed upward, do not treat. If the face is dark and there is sweating from the head, do not treat. If there is tightness in the heart and chest with inability to expel phlegm, do not treat. If there is diarrhea, do not treat.[23p]
Shortness of breath with limbs cold and not treated. Heart distressed, chest very red, tongue rolled, face red, eyes looking upward - not treated. Blood and qi attacking the heart, wanting to collapse, face red - not treated. Self-benefit, wheezing - not treated. Cold limbs - not treated. Alternating fever and delirium - not treated. Chest and abdomen distended and urgent - not treated. Throat sometimes feels thunderous or chokes on food - not treated. If a woman has contracted the cold with fever and throat pain, this indicates the menstrual flow is rising. The "Book of Living" states: When a woman has contracted cold, if her menstrual period arrives, she is clear during the day, but delirious in the evening, as if seeing spirits – this indicates heat has entered the blood chamber, without harming the stomach qi and the upper two jiaos, and should not be purged. Xiao Chai Hu Tang is the remedy. Now, if there is throat pain and alternating fever, with a red face and red lips, this indicates heat evil is obstructing upward.[24p]
Do not use Xiao Chai Hu Decoction; instead, it is advisable to use Bamboo Leaf and Gypsum Decoction to clear the upper jia and alleviate heart disturbances, which is quite effective. Following that, use Si Wu Decoction.

If a cold disease has persisted for four to five days with fever, dry nose, dry mouth, and sore throat, it indicates a disease of the Yangming channel. Yangming pertains to the stomach; excessive sweating can lead to the stomach's fluids drying up, which causes the saliva to dry and the throat to hurt. In this case, it is appropriate to use Ren Shen Bai Du San to treat it.

If the cold has lasted for three to five days and there is swelling in the throat that is bright red, with phlegm flowing out, as well as headache and stiff neck, this pertains to the Taiyang channel. The pathogenic qi has entered the meridians, affecting the heart, and the accumulated heat toxins attack the throat, resulting in swelling and pain. Add Burdock Seed, Original Ginseng, and Fresh Rehmannia to Gan Ju Decoction and administer the medicine in a similar manner.

If the cold has lasted for eight to nine days or more, with no heat present on the body, abdominal pain with diarrhea, and a sore throat, this indicates a disease of the Taiyin channel. If the cold has not been resolved after sweating and has shifted to Taiyin, and if there is fullness in the abdomen along with pain, diarrhea, and a swollen throat with a slightly pale color, this condition is treatable. If there is cold in the hands and feet, with persistent diarrhea, use Zhen Wu Decoction to treat it. The so-called Zhen Wu can nourish the lower source and support the Yang righteous qi, making the hands and feet warm, which is crucial.

The text states: "As long as the mouth is red and there is phlegm, treatment is possible." It is essential to adjust the medication based on the symptoms. If the mouth is black, it indicates the blood is already exhausted, with a hoarse voice and sweating; such a condition is untreatable. Careful examination of the symptoms is necessary.

If the cold has lasted for eight to nine days or more, with sweating that has not dispersed, a sore throat, dry tongue, and dry lips, this indicates a disease of the Shaoyin channel.[25p]
If the greater yin channel suffers from illness and, after sweating, it remains unresolved, it transmits into the lesser yin channel, which is associated with the kidneys. If there is excessive sweating, the kidney essence becomes depleted, and the kidney water is unable to moisten the throat, leading to this condition. Symptoms include diarrhea, abdominal pain, coldness in the hands and feet, and swelling and pain in the throat making swallowing difficult. If there is a lack of saliva and dryness on the tongue, it is not to be treated.

If a patient has been ill for eight or nine days with slight warmth in the body but no other symptoms, only throat pain without swelling, and hoarseness of voice, it should not be treated.

If a cold has lasted for more than ten days, and after sweating the illness has resolved without tidal fever, with a calm pulse and throat pain, this indicates residual toxicity attacking upward, for which a detoxifying decoction should be used.[26p]
If one is seriously affected by a severe illness, with symptoms such as a strong back, unbearable eye pain, urgent pain in the lower abdomen, a dark blue-black mouth, toxic qi overwhelming the heart, coldness in the limbs, nausea and vomiting, difficulty swallowing, and a deep, thin pulse, then prompt treatment should be administered by moxibustion below the navel. Recovery should occur within six days; otherwise, survival is unlikely.

In this case, external symptoms may resemble a snake coiling around the neck, with the body feeling hot and the head experiencing intense pain with swelling and discoloration. According to a comprehensive approach, the treatment should include blowing medicine with realgar and musk added. Taking Jing Fang Zhi Zi Er Chen Soup is necessary, along with urgent application of a goose feather dipped in thick oil from a lamp, stirring to remove phlegm until three to four bowls are cleared. If phlegm cannot be expelled, survival becomes difficult. It is essential to avoid wind.

Internal symptoms may present as red marks with white patches, showing obstruction and difficulty swallowing, all due to heat in the kidney channels, causing dryness and preventing moisture from rising, thus generating excessive heart fire and leading to this condition. One should take Bai Du San and employ the method of expelling vomit, continuing to use blowing medicine, repeating this three to five times. Additionally, the root of white pine should be crushed for its juice, used as a rinse to dispel wind-phlegm. If the throat opens producing a roaring sound, it is untreatable, and caution is advised.[27p]
Double Nipple Moth

The throat divides into two pathways, each receiving different ailments. The left throat is soft and concerns swallowing; the right throat is for speaking. The classic text states: the throat can distribute air, and the pharynx can swallow things. Therefore, diseases in the throat are collectively referred to as pharynx and throat. Physicians can treat them separately. The symptoms vary in types and appearances, and it is essential to examine them carefully.

The Double Nipple Moth, also known as the Double Moth Wind, consists of two growths on either side of the throat, the size of beans. Quickly administer a little yellow juiced, honey, mixed with Yuanming powder, gargle to dispel wind and phlegm. Then, take a decoction of Angelica and Forsythia, seven pills of realgar to clear toxins, and wash down with clear tea. Next, use Borneol powder and blow it in several times for immediate effect. Afterwards, take the Angelica and Forsythia decoction.

Single Nipple Moth

When the left side is affected by rising yang, swelling appearing slightly red signifies a blockage of lung qi, with external symptoms such as coldness in the hands and feet, spontaneous phlegm and saliva, dizziness, and blurry vision. Quickly administer a sour juice of sour vegetables mixed with Yuanming powder to clear phlegm; then blow in Borneol powder and follow with a decoction of Perilla Seed to reduce qi, Erchen Decoction, and Sweet Orange Decoction. If there is severe obstruction leading to loss of consciousness and breath, urgently ground Evodia into a paste and apply it to the soles of the feet.

For the right side, if the rising yang is slightly yellow, the shape resembles a silkworm cocoon, hence called the Nipple Moth. Symptoms also include coldness in the hands and feet, treated similarly. If there is accompanying back pain, add dried ginger and red peony root.[28p]
Alcohol Poisoning

Its shape resembles an egg, its swelling is bright red, its sheen like a mirror. Externally, it manifests as fever, aversion to cold, headaches, and stiffness in the neck. This indicates accumulated heat in the upper jiao, affecting the heart and spleen. The heart and spleen channels govern the upper jiao, so it is advisable to take a decoction of sticky seeds to counteract the poison, with the treatment remaining consistent. If the swelling is yellow, the blood is black, its shape resembles an arm, and the swelling appears like a pit, with external signs of a flushed face and upward gazing eyes, this indicates that heat poison is damaging the heart and spleen. The energies of the two channels connect to the mouth, circulating up and down, hence the sore throat. Treatment: first expel the phlegm, then use powdered ice to dry and blow into it, adding more dried ginger, tianhua powder, raw huanglian, gardenia fruit, forsythia, yuan shen, platycodon, and bitter orange to the mouse sticky seeds decoction.

Wind Poison

Externally red and swollen, internally slightly red with white, its shape resembles a steamed cake, with swelling and pain extending to the jaw. External manifestations include aversion to cold without fever, swelling in the jaw and face, and a tight jaw, indicating a clash of wind and phlegm obstructing the throat. The primary treatment must focus on expelling phlegm, using blown medicine. If there is external redness and swelling, apply a circumferential poultice, leaving a large opening in the center, and moisten it to enhance the medicinal effect.[29p]
Wind Heat

Swelling is red with a hint of purple, shaped like a fist; the person's face is red and the eyes look upwards. Externally, there are strong heat and aversion to cold, resembling a condition of cold damage. This illness arises from long accumulation of heat toxins, which is then exacerbated by wind. If the patient's voice is weak, it is advisable to use herbs that moisten the lungs for treatment. The color is bright red, and over time turns purple-red; urgently use a small (golden) knife to prick it, or a reed knife, allowing a small amount of blood to flow out, thus relieving the heat. Then continue taking decoctions and blow powdered borneol on it for significant effect. When the purple-red color changes to light red, recovery is imminent.

Yin Toxin

Swelling is like a purple plum and appears black; if the color is shiny and blood red, it can be treated; if the yin toxin is black, it cannot be treated. Externally, there is aversion to cold, the body quivers, and there is pain in the waist and cold in the feet; this occurs in winter due to invasion of dampness and interaction with fire evil. If the blood is slightly red and the swollen area is soft, and there is phlegm in the throat, it can be treated; if the blood is red-black with severe swelling and hardness, and the throat is dry, it is difficult to treat. First, take the Five Blessings Detox Pills, then use the Suzi Descend Qi Decoction, followed by blowing powdered borneol. Abstain from alcohol for a month.[30p]
Accumulated Heat Causing Abscess

The swelling appears like a yellow sugar plum, slightly yellow with red veins on top. There are external symptoms of pain in the neck and toothache, indicating heat in the stomach channel. The stomach energy connects to the throat, hence the throat abscess occurs. The method to expel phlegm is the same as before. Blow in medicine, using powdered borneol mixed with Yuanming powder; for decoction, add angelica and astragalus, with double the amount of honeysuckle.

Mute Phlegm Wind

This mute phlegm condition occurs when phlegm from wind invades between the throat and diaphragm, causing the inability to speak and locked jaws. Urgently use toad venom, ground into water and dropped into the nostrils to open it up. Then, drop tung oil into the throat, and use goose feathers to stir the wind and phlegm in the throat until it is expelled, after which use licorice soup to dispel the tung oil's influence, applying powdered borneol. Additionally, take Jingfang Baidu powder in three doses. If the face is purplish, tongue is bluish, lips are black, nose runs with cold mucus, nails are also blue, and the eyes tear excessively, treatment is not advisable.

Tongue Manipulation Wind

This symptom is an inability to speak, with the tongue protruding as the patient often twists it with their hands. Urgently use the cleft of both thumbs to prick with a three-edged needle, three pricks for each finger. If there is blood, it can be treated; if not, it cannot. In the lamp's wick oil, dip goose feathers to stir out phlegm. Furthermore, take seven pills of xionghuang detoxification pill, washed down with clear tea; after that, take a wind-dispersing licorice-citrus soup; finally, blow powdered borneol frequently.[31p]
Swelling and Closure

This poison arises from the spleen channels, due to the consumption of fried, oily foods, excessive drinking, and sexual activity, causing toxic gases to be unable to circulate and to accumulate at the root of the throat. If not treated promptly, the toxic closure may lead to sudden death. The treatment method is first to use vinegar water and juice to eliminate phlegm, then to apply throat-blowing medicine, blowing several times, followed by taking the Ba Zheng Shun Qi powder.

This condition arises in the middle of the sternum, initially appearing like a plum pit situated between the throat and diaphragm, unable to be expelled or swallowed. After three days, it gradually rises to the throat, known as a throat knot. This condition is caused by accumulated poison blocking the throat, with thick phlegm and fever. It is still divided into three sections: upper, middle, and lower. If the poison is in the lower section, it is difficult to treat; for the upper and middle sections, use throat-blowing medicine several times, followed by tea to wash it down; take seven pills of arsenic detoxification pill; then consume Shen Ling Shun Qi powder.

This condition results from heat and toxin affecting the heart channel, causing dryness in the throat without phlegm. If there is choking, treatment is not advisable. Use Chuanjisi Powder. If there is stabbing pain in the heart and lung area, continue with Danggui Lianqiao Powder and increase the dose of Dahuang for purgation. If left untreated for a long time, it can turn into a severe and deadly toxin that can harm life.

Emotion-Induced Abscess

This toxin arises from emotions such as joy, anger, worry, thought, sadness, fear, and shock, which injure the seven emotions, causing them to stagnate and form an abscess. The toxin then develops in the throat, and without prompt treatment, there is concern about the toxin attacking from within. If the throat bones protrude, pus will certainly emerge inside the mouth. Although it may not endanger life, it can lead to chronic conditions like a cold fistula. Use Shiqi Powder to treat it.

Heel Wind

This condition begins at the heel and extends to the throat, potentially recurring once a year or every six months. Avoid hot substances and do not be harmed by anger. The illness travels through one acupuncture point each day, and after seven days, seven points would be affected. Although it is not detrimental, it must be expressed. Use throat-soothing medicine and continue taking antidote powder. If there are foul-smelling bubbles, it can be fatal.

Throat Closure

This condition arises from external cold evil and internal heat harm, or from washing in hot water after a severe cold, forcing cold air into the lung channel, obstructing cold air in the middle jiao, and evil heat lodging in the heart channel, resulting in this illness. Urgently use a three-edged needle to prick the purple vein at the wrist or cause bleeding from the Shaoshang point; then use realgar detoxification pills crushed with cold tea for administration; also blow powdered Bingsh片 into the throat and wait for the expulsion of thick phlegm as a sign of recovery. Additionally, take Banzheng Junqi Powder first, and then Yushu Pill.[33p]
Focal Tumor

The throat tumors appear on either side of the throat, either single or double, resembling large round eyes, wrapped in blood vessels; hence they are named. This condition arises when the lung meridian is overheated, often due to excessive talking that damages qi, explosive shouting when angry, hurried recitation, excessive drinking of strong alcoholic beverages, or overeating roasted and grilled foods. If provoked, it causes pain; if not, there is no pain. It is essential to calm the mind and breathe gently, using medication to combat it, which will lead to the disappearance of this condition. Do not attempt to break it open with a knife; it is advisable to take nourishing qi and wind-dispelling decoction, and apply musk powder.

Suspended Abscess

This toxin forms in the upper palate, resembling a purple plum, and descends to the tongue. The person cannot speak, cannot extend the tongue, cannot lower the head, and must stand upright with the face up; red nasal discharge may occur. If not treated promptly, the toxin may penetrate into the brain, leading to death. The treatment involves using a copper spoon to open the mouth, and a bamboo needle to puncture the head of the abscess, cleaning it with salt water until all blood has been expelled. Ice powder is then blown into the affected area, and the mouth is closed to allow the medicine to work and be swallowed naturally. This process should be repeated three to five times; one should also take a decoction of Schizonepeta and Forsythia, followed by three pills of toxic transformation powder, and drink cold tea to cleanse. Despite appearing externally, this condition originates in the upper palate inside the mouth.[34p]
Throat Ulcer

A throat ulcer is caused by toxic qi from the heart and wind evil from the small intestine manifesting at the auditory orifice and penetrating the side of the thorax. It initially appears like a scrofula, where the sufferer cannot eat or drink, resulting in obstruction and difficulty. Gradually, it swells, ruptures, and purulently discharges. If treated early, recovery is possible. It is recommended to take herbal mixtures such as the Dang Gui and Lian Qiao powder, and internally use Borneol powder or Niu Huang Qing Xin Wan for treatment. Earthworms are not restricted; they can be mixed with musk and Borneol for topical application.

Residual Poison in Throat from Cold Damage

This condition arises from residual poison due to cold damage that does not dissipate, leading to a closure of the throat after eight or nine days. It is caused by heat poison entering the heart and spleen channels. Urgent medication includes Si Qi Decoction with two or three doses, followed by Borneol powder, and then the Quan Du Liu Qi Decoction.

Direct Pointer of the Ren School [Song Dynasty, Yang Shi Ying][35p]
One Principle, Many Particulars

The throat connects to the stomach, and the pharynx is an opening for lung qi. The throat swallows food, while the pharynx allows for the flow of qi. This unity is manifested in various distinctions.

Suspended Sore

A suspended sore in the throat is connected to vital areas; if the condition is not treated urgently, it can be fatal. The sore arises from the hard palate and is related to the throat. Therefore, if there is sudden swelling, it is also due to excessive heat.

Plum-pit Qi

When emotions are stagnant, phlegm and saliva accumulate, forming solid masses in the chest and abdomen that can block the throat like a plum pit. This prevents swallowing and leads to choking, harming the intake of food and drink. It is advisable to use the medicine "Si Qi Decoction." Men and women with this condition should avoid anger and cold foods.

Corpse Throat

Corpse throat arises from imbalanced yin and yang, excess spleen and lung energy, and the invasion of wind, heat, and toxins, which cannot circulate normally. This causes parasites to activate, eroding the throat, causing itching or pain, akin to symptoms of hidden pests within. It should be differentiated from conditions like typhus and treated accordingly.

Grain Thief

Grain thief refers to the sharp husks concealed within rice that, if mistakenly consumed, obstruct the throat and cannot be processed. Wind and heat combine with stagnant qi and blood, leading to swelling and pain. Urgent treatment is required, as it can also be fatal.

Pain

Throat pain occurs when wind evil invades the throat, causing qi stagnation and heat, resulting in pain.

Ulcers[36p]
A sore throat is caused by excess heat in the stomach area, which disrupts the three burners, manifesting as white heads and red roots. It is advisable to disperse the condition with sound.

Discussion on Treatment

The throat refers to the act of swallowing, while the larynx is related to the breath. The interaction between substances and air is contingent on the throat and larynx. When yin and yang are balanced, and the protective and nourishing energies are well-regulated, the pathways of qi flow freely. However, if one neglects nourishment, favors consuming minerals, indulges in overly roasted foods, or drinks excessively hot alcohol, it causes stagnation in the chest, leading to the accumulation of hot toxic energies that cannot be expelled, resulting in throat ailments. These ailments can present as swelling, pain, pharyngitis, or obstruction, leading to sores that cannot be swallowed or expelled, resembling flesh, all caused by wind, heat, and toxic energies. Additionally, there could be residual heat rising and burdening the soft palate, which may become enlarged. The soft palate pertains to the upper palate. There may also be cold in the internal organs, leading to an inability to swallow. Treatment should be approached with discernment.

The throat allows for the intake of substances, also known as the epiglottis. It is a critical passage for the flow of qi, connected to the stomach and governed by the earth's energies. The larynx is the space that allows for the passage of breath, connecting to the lungs and governed by heavenly energies. If the organ energies are balanced, illness does not arise; if they are imbalanced, with cold and heat leading to stagnation, disease develops. The key to treatment is to clear heat, warm cold, and harmonize the system when temperatures are neither hot nor cold according to the principles of classical texts.[37p]
Hanjian Six Writings by Liu Wanshu

Throat Obstruction

Throat obstruction: "Obstruction" means lack of sensation. It is often written as "closure," akin to blockage. Fire governs swelling, hence heat affects the upper part and causes swelling of the throat.

Ming Theory by Cheng Wujì

Pain, Itch, and Blockage

When the throat is not functioning well, it may either be painful or itchy, and one may be unable to eat, all resulting from toxic energy rising. The classics state: if a person with a Taiyang condition has a tight pulse, they will surely have throat pain; this happens as Taiyang evil strikes the Shaoyin. The Shaoyin pulse runs along the throat and surrounds the base of the tongue. In cases of Shaoyin throat pain, the pulse is floating and slow; there may be chilling symptoms, or diarrhea, which are also related to Shaoyin. It is inappropriate to induce sweating or purging. Use a mixture of Platycodon decoction or Pigskin decoction; in severe cases, add Banxia powder, Tongmai Sini decoction without Peony, but add Platycodon. If sweating does not stop, apply a warm powder. For ulcers in the throat where one cannot speak, use a bitter wine decoction. If a person suffers from cold damage for six to seven days followed by significant purging, with a deep and slow pulse, absent pulse in the wrists, throat issues, blood and pus in the saliva, and persistent cold extremities, it is difficult to treat. One should use a Mahuang Shengma decoction. In cases of kidney cold damage, usually resulting from unexpected cold damaging the Shaoyin channels, with headache and back pain, the pulse is weak, initially throat pain due to cold damage, followed by diarrhea and throat pain. Banxia Guizhi decoction is recommended, which is the same as Banxia Sini decoction. For throat blockage, use Wufan decoction. For oral ulcers that are red and rotting, soak Huangbo in honey and dissolve it in the mouth. If throat pain is severe, use Shengma Liuwu decoction.[38p]
Confucian Duty to Parents
(Yuan Dynasty, Zhang Congzheng)

Throat and Tongue Explanation

The throat and tongue function differently, much like various remedies. The pharynx and throat, epiglottis and tongue, are all part of the same system, yet their roles are distinct. The throat allows for the passage of air, thus connecting to the heavens; the pharynx facilitates swallowing, hence connecting to the earth. The epiglottis and throat work together to manage openings; when food descends, the epiglottis closes to prevent aspiration, and during breathing, it opens to release air, allowing the tongue to touch the hard palate, thus enabling the epiglottis to seal off the pharynx. These four components interact and are essential; if one is absent, the processes of eating and drinking cease, leading to death. These four are indeed the gates through which air and food enter and exit, hence the critical nature of the “seven orifices” mentioned in the “Nan Jing,” with the epiglottis functioning as the door for inhalation.

When ailments arise, they can be summarized in one word: fire. The “Nei Jing” states: "When yin and yang are in conflict, it is called throat obstruction." The commentary by Wang Taifu explains that "one yin" refers to the lesser yin of the hand, which is governed by the heart's fire; "one yang" refers to the lesser yang of the hand, related to the fire of the three heaters. Both fires govern the collaterals and channels in the throat; if heat accumulates, it leads to obstruction, and if obstruction worsens, it results in swelling, which can lead to blockage, ultimately resulting in death. The lesser yin of the foot follows the throat and envelops the root of the tongue, while the lesser yin of the hand encloses the pharynx; these two elements are indeed significant.[39p]
As for the pathways of the foot yangming which follow the throat, the foot taiyin which connects the pharynx to the root of the tongue, the hand taiyang which traverses the throat and descends into the diaphragm, and the foot jueyin which follows behind the throat—these meridians all mention the throat, yet the shaoyang does not refer to the throat. In the "Inner Canon," it speaks of one yin and one yang, referring to throat obstruction; why is this? It is because when people study the twelve meridians, many do not read the "Lingshu" text. The eleven chapters of the classic clearly record the principles of the twelve meridians, stating: The main pathway of the foot shaoyang circles the thigh and enters the hairline, connecting to the jueyin; the others enter the lateral costal region, follow through the chest, belong to the gallbladder, spreading above the liver, penetrating above the heart, and connect to the throat, emerging at the lower jaw. They scatter to the face, intertwine at the eyes, and connect the shaoyang to the outer canthus of the eyes.[40p]
The palm of the hand governs the heart, distinguishing it from the depths of the liquid three inches below, entering the chest, associated with the sanjiao, emerging through the throat and exiting behind the ears, merging beneath the bony region of the lesser yang. This is the qi of the hand's lesser yang sanjiao, combined with the qi of the heart's lesser yin, traveling through the throat. Examining the twelve meridians, only the foot taiyang diverges beneath the neck; the rest converge in the throat. Yet, why does the "Inner Canon" specifically mention the union of one yin and one yang resulting in throat obstruction? The essence lies in the governance of the two fires: when one prevails alone, it generates a heat-induced blockage, causing pain and rapidity. I argue that one can sum this up as fire. Therefore, in the twelve meridians, symptoms like throat dryness and pain, swelling of the pharynx, and strength at the base of the tongue, are all manifestations of the sovereign fire. Only the urgent throat obstruction arises from the fire of the minister. The sovereign fire resembles human fire; the minister fire resembles dragon fire. Human fire consumes wood slowly, while dragon fire does so rapidly. The "Inner Canon" refers to throat obstruction, which situates the pharynx and tongue in between, as their ailments are both related to fire, hence they are not distinctly separated.[41p]
In later times, physicians described various conditions in detail and established eight categories: single乳蛾 (milk moth), double乳蛾, single闭喉 (closed throat), double闭喉,子舌胀 (swollen sublingual),木舌胀 (swollen wooden tongue),缠喉风 (phlegm obstructing the throat), and走马喉闭 (rapid throat obstruction).

Heat rises and congests thin membranes beside the throat, causing swelling; this resembles milk moths—single or double in presentation. The smaller variant resembling milk moths is termed closed throat. If heat accumulates beneath the tongue, a small protrusion forms, called子舌胀. Heat accumulating in the middle of the tongue causes swelling, referred to as木舌胀. "Wood" signifies firmness without softness. When heat accumulates in the throat, swelling occurs externally, becoming both numb and itchy; if large, it is termed缠喉风. The condition of immediate death from throat obstruction is called走马喉痹.

Though these eight names are detailed, if they do not originate from heat, they are fundamentally different. Mild cases can be treated with softening methods, while severe cases require pungent dispersal; modern doctors have corresponding remedies such as mint, aconite, silkworms, white alum, and similar substances. As for走马喉痹, no such remedies are needed; it can swiftly lead to death. The most reliable method for treatment is bloodletting with a needle; once blood flows, the illness resolves. The Book of Changes states: "When blood is expelled, healing occurs."

In the past, I treated a woman with木舌胀, her tongue filling her mouth, and various medicines proved ineffective. I used a small, sharp needle for bloodletting, resulting in significant reduction in swelling after five or seven attempts; it took three days to fully return to normal. The amount of blood expelled was nearly a斗 (a measure).[42p]
I treated a man who had a swelling from throat wind, affecting both inside and outside, and he could not swallow medicine. I used cool medicine to irrigate his nose, administering it through more than ten lines. Externally, I applied a detoxifying powder. I ground equal parts of the Yangqi stone and dragon liver into a fine powder, washing it with fresh water a hundred times a day. After three days, the heat began to recede, and the swelling started to diminish.

I also treated a noblewoman for a throat blockage, which was also due to dragon fire. Although cool medicine was used, it could not be taken orally. Since it was dragon fire, it should be expelled with heat. The heat referred to is the cooking fire. I exposed her to the blazing sun and had her ascend to a high terrace, instructing her handmaid to carry a fire stove and place it over the medicine pot, keeping the medicine continuously very hot, but not boiling vigorously. She would sip it from time to time, over a hundred times, allowing the dragon fire to disperse. This method utilizes heat to counteract cold, thus avoiding the conflict with heat illness.[43p]
In general, treating throat phlegm by drawing blood with needles is the most effective method. However, people fear needles, and seeking alternatives can lead to immediate death. If there are needle wounds from using needles, it is advisable to crush a piece of fresh ginger and mix it with hot white soup, sipping on it periodically to help the wound close easier. The "Copper Man" also mentions moxibustion, but it is only suitable for mild cases; for severe cases, delay may be deadly. Therefore, treating the fire of throat phlegm should be treated with urgency, akin to extinguishing a fire. The "Inner Canon" states that when fire is stagnated, it must be released, referring to inducing sweat. However, how can one induce sweating in the throat? Thus, drawing blood is a form of inducing sweat. Future practitioners should not cling to narrow methods, claiming that their treatment does not affect the internal organs, which is superior to bloodletting. If they are fortunate enough to succeed with minor ailments, they may unfortunately encounter serious illnesses and face fatal consequences. Let there be no regret afterwards.[44p]
Danxi Heart Method
(Yuan Dynasty, Zhu Zhenheng)

Pain from Throat Obstruction

Throat obstruction is generally due to phlegm-heat; for severe cases, use tung oil to induce vomiting. Sore throat with ulcers is due to deficiency heat. Blood deficiency often leads to false fire, wandering unrestrained, affecting the throat. Use ginseng, schisandra, and honey-fried gentian. For false fire, use ginseng and bamboo juice. For blood deficiency, use the Four Substances with bamboo juice. For excess heat, use huanglian (Coptis chinensis), schisandra, mint, and saltpeter, mixed with honey and ginger juice to dissolve and gargle; alternatively, take some clean, finely ground dandelion root, mix it with a little good wine, and drip it into the throat for immediate relief from pain. For throat pain, schisandra must be used; for yin deficiency fire rising, use codonopsis. For sore throat, mix borax with alun, white silkworm, and white plum meat to gargle; again, schisandra and codonopsis must be used.[45p]
Throat Wind

Throat wind is associated with phlegm heat. Dai Sigong states that when both the inside and outside of the throat are swollen, it is so. Throat wind, and the symptoms of throat closure, arise from the presence of phlegm and saliva in the diaphragm or from unregulated alcohol, lust, and emotions. When fire agitates the phlegm and obstructs the throat, it leads to swelling and pain both internally and externally, making it impossible for fluids to be ingested; this can be considered dangerous and urgent. The symptoms of throat wind appear first with a tight feeling in the chest and diaphragm, shortness of breath, and suddenly swelling and pain in the throat, along with coldness in the hands and feet, leading to obstructed breath if left untreated for even a moment.

Breast Moth

The single moth wind appears round, about the size of a small chopstick head, located above the throat, either on the left or right side, and is difficult to treat below the throat. The double moth wind consists of two similar round formations on either side of the throat, also about the size of a small chopstick head, which is likewise difficult to treat below.

Throat Wind

Throat wind is identified by red coloration from the area around the jaw to beneath the jaw. Generally, both the inside and outside being swollen indicates throat wind. In cases of throat closure, where toxic energy returns to the heart, leading to fullness in the chest, accelerated breath, and persistent diarrhea from below, it is fatal.

Suspended Abscess

Suspended abscess is referred to as "Emperor's Bell." When the abscess is swollen and hangs down several inches, it is called "Emperor's Bell Wind." It is advisable to use a salt and alum powder; it should not be pricked, as doing so can be fatal.[46p]
Medical Treatise: An Overview

The "Inner Canon" states: The convergence of one Yin and one Yang is called throat obstruction. Wang's commentary explains that one Yin refers to the Jueyin liver and the pericardium, while one Yang refers to the Shaoyang gallbladder and the Sanjiao. All four channels contain the relative fire. Shuhe stated that the gallbladder and Sanjiao seek fire treatment, while the liver and pericardium are no different. Dongyuan remarked that fire and vital energy do not coexist; where one prevails, the other diminishes. When vital energy is deficient, relative fire can arise, causing sudden outbreaks of throat obstruction and similar ailments.

The epiglottis, referred to as the 'door of breath' in the classics, is a crucial gateway for the elevation and descent of respiration in the human body. When there is sudden swelling and pain, with water and liquid unable to enter, and speech hindered, death can occur in an instant, which is truly alarming. Swelling on both sides of the epiglottis is colloquially known as "double breast moth," which is easy to treat. Swelling on one side is called "single breast moth" and is difficult to treat.

Ancient formulas referred to throat obstruction, which is caused by the rebellion of relative fire. The classics say: One water cannot overcome two fires; moreover, two waters cannot overcome five fires. This suggests the ease with which true water can be depleted and relative fire can become active. For instance, great anger can cause fire to rise from the liver, sexual indulgence can cause fire to rise from the kidneys, and irregular diet can incite fire from the spleen and stomach. Thus, fire is the root of phlegm, and phlegm is the manifestation of fire. Fire is characterized by its rapid nature, hence illnesses can erupt violently.[47p]
The method of treatment must first involve expelling the phlegm, or using a gold needle to puncture the swollen area; this is an urgent, symptomatic treatment. When using medicine, one must adhere to the treatment principles from the "Inner Canon," employing herbs such as Platycodon, Licorice, Scrophularia, Cimicifuga, Saposhnikovia, Notopterygium, Schizonepeta, Ginseng, Atractylodes, and Poria, with a small addition of dried Ginger and Aconite, administered gradually and frequently, never taken in a single dose. This is the fundamental method of treatment. One must absolutely avoid taking cold and cooling medicines, as not only are they unhelpful, but they may also hasten death. The common people are often unaware of this principle and hastily resort to strong herbs like Scutellaria, Coptis, Gardenia, and Rhizoma Picrorhiza, believing they are treating the condition. Worse yet, they mix in very bitter and cold medicines, taking them frequently and in large doses, perceiving only a slight reduction in swelling or slightly improved speech, celebrating the effects with the physician, unaware that the underlying heat has not been resolved while cold has re-entered, allowing toxins to invade the abdomen, which may ultimately lead to persistent cough, becoming untreatable—how lamentable this is!

There is an external condition called "big head disease," commonly known as "pinched head plague," which is quite severe, with a mortality rate of eight or nine out of ten among those infected. Treatment should focus on regulating Qi, and the methods are not vastly different. A remarkable remedy is the "Universal Detoxifying Drink" by Dongyuan, proven to be effective, deserving of thorough study and expansion by practitioners, as it aims to save lives in this world, which is indeed fortunate![48p]
Essentials of Diagnosis and Treatment
[Ming Dynasty - Dai Sigong]

Swelling and Pain

For sore throat, sweet mandarin peel decoction (Ganji Tang) is recommended. If heat toxin attacks upward, with or without sores, and sweet mandarin peel decoction is ineffective, add a small amount of schizope, called "Holy Decoction." Alternatively, in the Holy Decoction, add one part forsythia and half a part of euphorbia, or use sweet dew drink, along with Bingyun powder, prepared and consumed with salted water to nourish the body's essence, in conjunction with peppermint and chicken-suet pills to dissolve in the mouth.

If sore throat worsens with cold remedies, use ginger juice.
For internal heat manifesting in the upper jiao causing throat pain, use phellodendron bark, coptis, and rhubarb, ground into powder, mixed with water, applied to the soles of the feet and the affected area, as per "Ye's Prescriptions."

For throat pain due to heat obstructing, or coughing with blood, use Jinfeicao powder, supplemented with cinnabar phlegm-dissolving pills. If throat pain does not improve with all cooling medicines, use Zhi Nan decoction.

For throat obstruction causing pain, swelling, and inability to speak, with foreign sensation in the throat (named "throat wind"), use sweet mandarin peel decoction. If heat obstructs the upper jiao, causing sore throat, and swallowing dry substances feels less moist than usual, with a dry mouth while sleeping, use Holy Decoction with half a part of ginseng and seven parts of original ginseng, or be supplemented with Bingyun powder and chicken-suet pills.

For concurrent upper obstruction and irritability in the heart, use the five spirit powder with cinnabar. In cases of upper obstruction, it is also advisable to crush sand shell into ash, preserve its essence, grind into powder, and take it mixed with water.[49p]
Medical Treatise 【Ming Dynasty - Lou Ying】

Regarding Pain and Sores from Obstruction

The term "throat obstruction" refers to the inability to breathe properly through the throat, resulting in a blockage of speech and air. The term for "throat pain" and "pharyngeal pain" indicates the throat's incapacity to swallow saliva and food, associated with blockages of the earth's energy. "Throat obstruction combined with pharyngeal pain" denotes an illness affecting both the throat and pharynx, leading to blockage of both celestial and earthly energies. It is evident that one suffering from throat obstruction must also experience pharyngeal pain, while those with isolated pharyngeal pain cannot simultaneously suffer from throat obstruction.

Throat obstruction accompanied by aversion to cold, and a weak pulse at the wrist, are considered exterior symptoms. In such cases, it is appropriate to use sweet tangerine decoction or a mixture of pinellia, cinnamon twig, and licorice to address the aspects of cold, heat, and dispersion. If one is unable to consume liquids, use the detoxifying xionghuang pill (realgar pill), grinding four or five pills in highly sour vinegar, administering it into the mouth, and then expectorate the thick phlegm.
