Follow this by sucking on the natural juice of fresh ginger, which has a remarkable effect.[50p]
In cases of throat obstruction accompanied by chills, it is caused by cold defeating heat—cold confined externally and heat stagnating internally. Ginger juice disperses the external cold, allowing the internal heat to be released and thus lead to recovery. One must avoid using bile and copper sulfate, which are cold agents applied to the throat, as they can cause the yang to stagnate and not extend; also to avoid using cooling agents like nitre and yellow sulfur, as they would lead to the sinking of yang into the interior, resulting in disaster in no time. Han Zhihe states that when the pulse at the inch is weaker than that at the guan and chi, it is necessary to dissipate yin and assist yang. Dongyuan states that when the pulse at the two inches is insufficient, it indicates a deficiency of yang qi; thus, exterior medications are used to lift its energy to support yang. If all three positions have small and weak pulses, the same method can be applied.

Throat obstruction, which is common in rural areas, generally resembles one another, as they belong to the malady of the atmospheric influence of heaven. Therefore, treatment must first disperse the exterior, and it is highly forbidden to apply sour medicines or cold medicines, as they would cause the evil to remain internally and not be released. There are two types of illness: The first belongs to fire. The classic states: "The lesser yang leads to throat obstruction." It also states that the lesser yang governs the affairs of heaven; when the summer heat arrives, the people suffer from throat obstruction. Treatment should follow Zhongjing’s syrup of platycodon. If there are red spots on the face, it indicates yang toxin, and one should utilize remedies for yang toxin to induce sweating. The second belongs to dampness.[51p]
The Classic says: The victory of the Taiyin leads to the internal accumulation of fire energy, causing throat obstruction. Additionally, it states: The Taiyin in the spring is overcome by excessive dampness, resulting in swelling of the throat and throat obstruction. The treatment should be to use a decoction of Banxia, Guizhi, and Gancao for the vitality of the person. If the face is bluish-black, it pertains to Yin poison, and it is suitable to sweat out the Yin poison using various prescriptions.

In the spring of the fifth year of Hongwu, there were many cases of throat obstruction in the villages, which was due to the qi at the end of the previous year and the beginning of this year, the two fires causing evils. I repeatedly used the Ganju Decoction with added Huanglian, Banxia, Jiangcan, and Shucan roots to induce sweating. For those with deficiency, I added Ren, Qishi, and Gui. If liquids do not enter, I first used the Detoxifying Xionghuang Pills, ground with vinegar and administered to the throat; phlegm would emerge, and then I would use fresh ginger juice to administer it again, using the above-mentioned medicine, all would be remarkably effective. However, if one uses acidic and cold treatments such as alum, they will not be curative, as the evil remains trapped within.

In cases of throat obstruction without aversion to cold, and when the pulse at the cun is large, slippery, and solid at the Guanchu, they all pertain to lower conditions.[52p]
It is appropriate to use cooling herbs such as nitrate and indigo to lower conditions, or astringents like alum to gather them. Han Zhihe said: If the pulse at the inch is larger than that at the guan and chi, it is advisable to disperse yang and assist yin. Dongyuan states: If the two-inch pulse is solid, it indicates an excess of yin and a deficiency of yang; if treated, it will improve. Therefore, I often employ this method to treat acute throat obstruction, as one would respond to a drum. If all three positions are solid, this method can also be applied.

In cases of acute throat obstruction, if the voice resembles snoring, as if there is phlegm resonating in the throat, this indicates a severe condition of the lungs. Immediate use of ginseng paste is necessary, consumed with ginger juice or bamboo juice. If ginseng paste is not available, first boil ginseng soup for relief. Taking it early leads to an almost full recovery; later, it results in a partial recovery and, if delayed, only minimal improvement.

For throat pain, there is a significant deficiency of yin and an excessive escaping of yang, with phlegm accumulating above, leading to the pain. The pulse must be floating and large, with a heavy touch yielding a roughness. Immediate treatment should restore balance between yin and yang, using only ginseng, boiled to a rich decoction and consumed slowly.

Throat ulcers tend to have excessive fire, roaming without restraint, troubling the throat. It is advisable to use ginseng, honey-fried yellow bitter herb, and schizonepeta to treat it.[53p]
Introduction to Medicine
(Ming Dynasty - Li Chen)

Throat Diseases Belong to Fire

The respiration and the intake and output of food through the throat are the gateways of the human body. In later generations, there are eighteen named types of throat diseases, which, although diverse, all return to the element of fire. This is because the lesser yin provides the sovereign fire, and the lesser yang provides the ministerial fire; these two channels converge in the throat. If the sovereign fire is weak, it leads to heat accumulation, resulting in pain and swelling. If the ministerial fire is strong, it results in severe swelling and insensitivity, potentially leading to obstruction that may result in death. Hence, it is said: “The union of one yin and one yang leads to throat obstruction.” Both the liver and pericardium belong to yin, while the gallbladder and sanjiao belong to yang; all four channels have ministerial fire. Fire is the origin of phlegm, and phlegm is the manifestation of fire. Therefore, when mentioning fire, phlegm is inherently present; and when speaking of the throat, the teeth and tongue are also included.[54p]
Fire Differentiates Between Reality and Illusion

Real fire is caused by overeating fried and roasted foods, leading to the accumulation of heat and toxins, resulting in thirst, constipation, phlegm, and wind attacking upwards, which can cause throat obstruction. There must be three days of discomfort in the chest and diaphragm, with a tight and rapid pulse. The treatment should first eliminate wind and phlegm, followed by detoxifying heat, cooling the diaphragm with a formula adding Huang Lian (Coptis), Jing Jie (Schizonepeta), and Shi Gao (Gypsum). Alternatively, one can use Gu Jing Huang Decoction, Fang Feng Tong Sheng Powder, or San Huang Pills to dissolve in the mouth. If wind dries the throat making it parched and spiky, causing difficulty in swallowing, use Bai Du San with added Huang Qin (Scutellaria), Ban Xia (Pinellia), and increase the amount of Jie Geng (Platycodon), Bo He (Mint), and Sheng Jiang (Ginger) for decoction. If phlegm is excessive, add Shi Gao. For these medications, take them at midday or later. If there is vomiting or damage due to consuming hot foods and prickly grains, along with swelling and pain from wind-heat clashing with blood and qi, use Xiao Feng San adding Bo He, Yuan Shen, and Quanfeng, or She Gan Decoction or Niu Bang Zi Decoction. For a heavy tongue, it is like a sacred golden ingot. For swelling at the root of the tongue, use She Xiang Zhu Sha Wan.[55p]
For those experiencing sore throat, use the Puji Xiaodu drink. Excess heat from drinking alcohol stirs the spleen's fire; anger stirs the liver's fire; lust stirs the kidney's fire. When the fire rises and attacks, the throat and esophagus become dry, but urination remains normal, with a faint pulse in the lesser yin. Treatment should focus on tonifying deficiency and lowering heat. For those with blood deficiency, use Siwu Decoction with additional Platycodon, Schizonepeta, Anemarrhena, and Coptis; for those with qi deficiency, use Si Junzi Decoction with added Licorice, Platycodon, Radical Scrophulariae, and Cimicifuga, possibly with dry ginger and Aconite as guiding herbs, taken gradually. If phlegm is excessive, add a fresh fish gallbladder to Erchen Decoction, prepared with glutinous rice and dried into powder, and taken with ginger juice; consider also the Tanhutu or Qianjin decoctions. For those who have previously taken cooling medicines and have sound issues, use the Secret Transmission Decoction to regulate qi.

For sudden cold-induced throat constriction, use Chaiqiao Banxia Decoction or Pigskin Decoction. For kidney-related cold and yin conditions, use Banjiao Decoction with honey and Aconite.

Common remedies include Ganjiao Decoction, Ligao Decoction, Bingmei Pill, and Rhinoceros Horn and Amber Ointment; alternatively, use a single herbal powder mixed with honey to form pills the size of peanuts, taking three pills with freshly drawn water.

Generally, cooling medicines should not be used alone for the throat. A rapid effect may mask residual heat, leading to renewed cold symptoms. When toxic qi invades the abdomen, it can cause swelling in the chest, shortness of breath, diarrhea, and cyanosis of the hands and feet. If after seven days one cannot eat and the mouth resembles that of a fish, it can lead to death.[56p]
Jiao Tu Method

Jiao Method: Use powdered bile from a blue fish three times, and the swelling will disperse.
Tu Method: Use the bile of a blue fish in winter, mixed with dry alum; when in use, add some finely roasted herbal powder and a little salt, mixed with vinegar, and use a goose feather to dip in the medicine to induce vomiting until all phlegm is expelled. If fish bile is not available, use half a pound of white alum and ten pieces of croton seed meat, combined with dry alum, then remove the croton, and induce vomiting; this is remarkably effective. After vomiting, use a golden key to blow it; regularly drinking sweet orange soup is most excellent. If the jaw is tightly clenched, use a jaw-opening medicine afterward, or two immortal powder; for those who are unconscious, use a one-character powder.

Expelling Fire through Sweating

"Expelling fire through sweating" means to induce sweat. Throat ulcers should avoid sweating to prevent worsening the condition. Only when using a needle to draw blood is the essence of sweating applicable. If a lot of blood is drawn, healing occurs. For those with needle sores, ginger juice mixed with warm water should be sipped at intervals. If the patient fears needles, apply a gentle needle technique. In cases where there are severe blood blisters on the upper body and none visible on the lower body, have the patient hold a mouthful of water and use a sharpened bamboo tube to prick the nostril and draw blood, which is effective. However, for those who have kidney damage from cold or swollen with Emperor's bell, needles should be avoided. Burn snake bed seeds in a bottle, and have the patient inhale the smoke into the throat for healing.[57p]
Switching Method

Xionghuang Detox Pills, Longnao Poision Dispelling Powder, Yuyue Key; alternatively, use the oil from the seeds of ba dou (croton seed) pressed on oil paper to light a wick, then blow it out to produce smoke, which is inhaled through the nose for immediate effect, causing saliva to flow from the mouth and nose, and opening the teeth. One method uses the flesh of ba dou wrapped in cotton and inserted into both nostrils, which ensures a clear passage. This method employs ba dou to treat 'running horse throat obstruction', attacking heat with heat, as heat promotes circulation.

Throat Obstruction and Loss of Voice

For throat obstruction and loss of voice, use the secret recipe of Jiangqi Decoction with the addition of dried tangerine peel and Huangqin (Scutellaria baicalensis). For loss of voice due to wind-cold, use Ganqiao Decoction with Hezi fruit and Mutong, supplemented with fresh Rehmannia juice for moisture; or Hezi Powder. For blood deficiency leading to voice hoarseness, use Qingdai and He powder mixed with honey to dissolve in the mouth; or Lung Nourishing Pills with honey and grease simmered. If ordinary voice clarity is compromised, add Gui Ben Pills. For internal injury and atrophic throat issues causing loss of voice, no treatment method is available.[58p]
Remarkable and Effective Formulas
(Ming Dynasty, Fang Xian)

General Discussion

Dai Ren Yun: The throat and the larynx, the epiglottis and the tongue, these four exist within one system, yet their causes differ. The throat is for taking in air, thus the throat's air communicates with heaven; the larynx is for taking in food, thus the larynx's air communicates with the earth. The epiglottis and the larynx work in conjunction to control opening and closing; when food descends, it is sucked in and covered, and when air rises, it is exhaled. Hence, when the tongue presses against the hard palate, the epiglottis can close off the throat. These four interact in function; if one is missing, eating and drinking cease, leading to death. These four are the portals for the circulation of air and food, being in the most critical area, which is why they cause illness; signs of throat pain and laryngeal obstruction are difficult to treat. Mild cases may be cured through treatment, but severe cases often result in peril. The "Inner Canon" states: "A blockage of one yin and one yang is termed laryngeal obstruction." Wang's commentary states that one yin refers to the Hand Shaoyin’s Heart channel, while one yang refers to the Hand Shaoyang’s San Jiao channel. Both fires govern the channels and are interconnected in the larynx; when air is hot, it can lead to internal blockages, which, if severe, cause swelling; excessive swelling leads to obstruction, and if obstruction becomes extreme, it can result in death. It's not just these two channels causing this illness; according to the twelve channels, only the Foot Taiyang diverges below the neck, while the others converge at the throat. Hence, when the two fires (the Ruler and Officer) dominate, the heat causes blockages, leading to pain and rapid onset.[59p]
In the twelve meridians, pain in the throat, swelling in the jaw, and swelling of the tongue are primarily caused by the Emperor Fire. However, a sudden closure of the throat is attributed to the Minister Fire. The Emperor Fire is akin to human fire; the Minister Fire is similar to dragon fire. Human fire burns wood slowly; dragon fire burns wood rapidly. The texts state that a throat obstruction involves both the throat and tongue, and since the affliction is due to fire, they are not differentiated. Later scholars should examine its details; here are eighteen symptoms of throat and pharynx disorders:

  1. Single Wind (Dan E Feng) - appears as a round shape about the size of a small chopstick head near the upper throat; it can appear on either side and can be treated; those appearing lower are difficult to treat.
  2. Double Wind (Shuang E Feng) - two round shapes, each about the size of a small chopstick, appearing on either side of the throat; those appearing lower are difficult to treat.
  3. Cicada Tongue Wind (Chan She Feng), also known as "Re-grown Tongue" - a second tongue regenerating from below the original tongue.
  4. Toothworm Wind (Ya Qi Feng) - swelling on the gums leading to pus-filled sores.
  5. Wood Tongue Wind (Mu She Feng) - the tongue gradually enlarges, resembling a cooked pig tongue, unable to move.
  6. Yellow Tongue Wind (She Huang Feng) - swelling and pain on the tongue with a yellow color.
  7. Biting Teeth and Locking Wind (Yao Ya Jin Feng) - teeth at the end become gnarled, and the mouth cannot open.
  8. Fish Mouth Wind (Yu Kou Feng) - resembles a fish sucking water and is untreatable.
  9. Gathered Toxins Blocking Throat Wind (Ju Du Se Hou Feng) - toxins gathered in the throat with thick saliva, causing chills and fevers; those above can be treated legally, but those below are difficult to treat.[60p]
    Ten: The suspended Qi poison wind causes swelling around the eyes, difficulty swallowing water, and external swelling resembling hen's eggs.

Eleven: The choking food wind, also known as the flying silk poison, causes the mouth to foam when consuming foul-smelling raw food.

Twelve: The hunting cheek wind results in swelling of the cheeks, breaking swelling where the teeth have worn down.

Thirteen: The winding throat wind manifests as redness below the jaw; it can also exhibit extreme cold or heat, posing a serious danger.

Fourteen: The pine nut wind fills the mouth, causing the throat to be red like pig liver; when one opens the mouth to swallow, the breath is obstructed, leading to an inability to eat or drink. Blow-throat medicine can be used, or apply medicinal powder to the swollen area. If mild, it will recede; if severe, there will be rapid throat obstruction, which can be fatal if untreated.

Fifteen: The collapsing sand sweet mouth wind causes the gums under the tongue to swell red, and the mouth feels hot, resembling soup; if the gum condition worsens, it may result in tooth loss.

Sixteen: The linked pearl wind starts under the tongue, initially appearing as one, then another; in severe cases, three, five, seven, or nine linked pearls may form.

Seventeen: The bee venom appears as itching and sores on the cheeks or under the tongue, resembling a yellow color like a bee.

Eighteen: The traveling scrofula wind causes multiple swollen lymph nodes on the neck, with skin redness and swelling, resulting in cold and heat sensations.

Only the wooden tongue indicates stiffness without softness. Heat accumulates in the throat, swelling externally, causing numbness and itching, and a significant swelling is known as the winding throat wind. Sudden throat paralysis leading to rapid death is referred to as the galloping horse throat paralysis.[61p]
Although the eighteen types of ailments are distinct in name, their treatment should not be far removed from the concept of fire. Minor ailments can be alleviated with softness, while more serious ones can be resolved with sharpness. For treating these conditions, the world has methods such as mint, aconite, silkworms, alum, nitrum, and verdigris. As for the throat affliction caused by running horse, what need is there for these remedies? The difference between life and death is as close as a person's palm. The least harmful method is bloodletting with a needle; once blood flows, the illness is resolved. Yet, people fear needles and seek other means. If one persists in this, they risk losing their life in an instant. When using needles, if one chokes, it is advisable to crush a piece of fresh ginger and mix it with hot white soup to sip occasionally, which will mitigate the choking. Treating throat afflictions is akin to firefighting; it cannot be taken lightly. According to various texts, for a swollen tongue, urgently use a small and sharp needle to draw blood five to seven times to alleviate the condition. For wind swelling in the throat that cannot be relieved by medicine, instill cool medicine through the nose to expel it, while also applying a detoxifying poultice outside; once heat diminishes, the swelling will subside. Throat afflictions are related to dragon fire; even when using cooling agents, one should frequently sip on an intensely hot decoction. This medicine acts with heat to guide out the cold, not as a rejection of heat illnesses. Additionally, frequently pricking the Lesser Shang point with a small needle to draw blood can lead to recovery. Future practitioners must distinguish between human fire and dragon fire ailments; effective treatments will follow.[62p]
Six Essentials of Medical Principles (Ming - Zhang Sanxi)

Throat Obstruction

The throat swallows substances, while the larynx awaits the wind; its essence is clear and void, allowing no trace of turbidity. The "Nanjing" states: the qi of the three jiao connects to the throat, hence vocal sounds arise. Nevertheless, the three jiao pertains to the fire of the yang, and fire leads to diseases appearing rapidly, thus a sudden swelling in the throat is called "throat obstruction" in ancient texts. There may also be phlegm-fire rising from the stomach, causing obstruction in the patient. Generally, if it arises abruptly, it must be phlegm-fire, and the urgent remedy is to induce vomiting, while needling to dispel toxic blood is superb. Those ignorant are fearful and hesitant, often leading to unfortunate outcomes, showcasing a lack of understanding of the correct principles.

Xue's Medical Cases (Ming - Xue Ji)

Obstruction Pain Syndromes

Master Danxi said: throat pain is due to blood deficiency, treated with Si Wu Decoction plus bamboo juice; for yin deficiency with rising fire, one must use Yuan Shen; for qi deficiency, add ginseng and bamboo juice. Furthermore, for swelling and pain in the throat, if there is yin deficiency and yang energy surging, with phlegm binding above, the pulse must be floating and large, while the heavy pulse should be thin. To expel the dead, one should use ginseng decocted strongly and drunk slow. If one treats it with methods for solid symptoms, the calamity is at hand. This is something previously unrecognized by others, saving countless lives from premature demise. Additionally, I mention the conditions related to upper jiao wind-heat and bladder yin deficiency briefly afterward. Pain or cold and heat indicate the pathogen is at the surface, thus it should be dispersed. For swelling, pain, and an abundance of phlegm and saliva, the pathogen is above.[63p]
If there is pain with a rapid and weak pulse, it indicates a deficiency of Yin; one should nourish Yin and clear heat. If there is swelling, pain, fever, and constipation, this indicates a condition of excess both inside and outside; one should resolve the exterior and attack the interior. If the symptoms are urgent, one may puncture the affected area or needle the Shaoshang point.

Mr. Xiaoshan says: In cases of throat obstruction without aversion to cold, with a pulse that is large and slippery at the cun and guan positions, these indicate a lower condition; it is advisable to use cold medicines such as Niter or Indigo to reduce it, or sour agents like copper sulfate to collect it. Mr. Han Zhihe states: If the cun pulse is larger than the guan and chi pulses, one should disperse Yang and assist Yin. Mr. Dongyuan notes: Both cun pulses being solid indicates excessive Yang and deficient Yin; by purging it, one can promote recovery. Therefore, I respect this method for treating the aforementioned conditions, akin to the response of a drum.

Chen Zangqi often treats interior cold and throat obstruction, causing difficulty in swallowing and expectoration, using prepared Aconite without skin and navel, coated with honey and roasted, so that the honey can enter; one should hold it in the mouth without swallowing. It is said to be very effective.

Meiheqi

Meiheqi refers to a sensation of blockage in the throat, where one cannot cough it out or swallow it down, resembling a plum pit. This is caused initially by excess joy and anger, which accumulates heat and leads to phlegm and fluid stagnation, resulting in this ailment. One should use a modified version of the Siqi Decoction and a modified version of the Erchen Decoction.[64p]
Phlegm-Heat in the Throat

Heat accumulates in the throat, causing swelling around the outside, resulting in numbness and itchiness. Severe swelling is termed "Wind Phlegm in the Throat." If the throat is closed and suddenly leads to death, it is called "Running Horse Throat Phlegm."

Phlegm-Heat arises when heat rises and affects both sides of the throat, creating external swelling. It resembles the shape of a butterfly, with one side being singular and the other double. The smaller variety of this phlegm is called "Throat Closure."

Guidelines for Diagnosis and Treatment (Ming Dynasty, Wang Kentang)

Throat Abscess

If one asks about the occurrence of abscesses on both sides of the throat, the response is: This is called "夹疽" (Throat Abscess), which pertains to the Heart Channel of the Lesser Yin, the Spleen Channel of the Greater Yin, and the Liver Channel of the Jueyin, resulting from hot toxic energies rising. It is advisable to use amber and rhinoceros horn ointment, rhinoceros horn powder, Huanglian Disinfectant Decoction, and Huoming Decoction with added Yan Shen, Jie Geng, and Huang Lian. Those with internal suppuration are difficult to treat. If there is rising fire from deficiency and phlegm blockage with an inability to eat, death may ensue.

Throat Carbuncle

If one asks about the occurrence of a carbuncle in the throat, the response is: It is termed "Throat Carbuncle," also known as "Severe Carbuncle." Due to its intense heat and toxicity, it is fearsome. It belongs to the Ren Channel as well as the Hand Taiyang and Hand Shaoyin, resulting from accumulated heat and worry. It is urgent to clear heat and attack toxins, using amber and rhinoceros horn ointment, Huanglian Disinfectant Decoction, Ziyin Dan, and Wujin San as options. For those who are robust, one gold pill should be administered. If treatment is delayed and it ruptures through the throat, it may lead to death.[65p]
Discussion of Swelling and Pain in the Throat

The throat and the pharynx are not the same. The throat is the gateway for breathing from the lungs, primarily responsible for exhalation rather than inhalation; the pharynx is the pathway for food and water from the stomach, primarily responsible for inhalation rather than exhalation. The throat and pharynx regulate breathing and control ascending and descending, acting as critical gateways of the body. The classics say: "The illness arising from the foot's lesser yin manifests as thirst, dry tongue, swollen pharynx, shortness of breath, dry throat, and pain." The "Su Wen" states: "Evil influences on the foot's lesser yin channels cause swelling and pain in the throat, preventing food intake." Additionally, it says: "The channels of the foot's lesser yin run through the throat and connect to the root of the tongue." Therefore, any throat pain is a disease of the lesser yin, with distinctions of cold, heat, deficiency, and excess. The fire of the lesser yin surges upward like galloping horses, clashing at the throat where the energies are tightly locked. This causes the qi to become stagnant, resulting in swelling or pain. The symptoms must include internal heat, dry mouth, reddened face, and phlegm surging upward; the pulse at the wrist will be rapid yet weak. This is due to the depletion of kidney water, leaving the fire of the yuan (original) unchecked. One must use a large dose of Six-Flavor Rehmannia, Asparagus, and Five-Flavor remedy to be taken as a decoction. If there is excessive desire leading to depletion of the original yang with unrooted fire wandering uncontrolled in the throat, one must use a large dose of Eight-Flavor Kidney Qi Pill, decocted and cooled to drink, to draw fire back to its source for a chance of rescue. This treatment method for throat pain due to yin deficiency aligns with what Zhu says about treating upper body diseases by addressing the lower body.[66p]
The throat of a person resembles a curved pipe; when the fire burns within, if water is poured in from above, the pipe will explode violently. Only below the stove, when a basin of water is reflected, the above fire will extinguish; this is one proof of treating an upper ailment by addressing the lower part.

Among these conditions, there are milk worms and throat worms, which have different names. Swelling on both sides of the throat is called double worm, while swelling on one side is called single worm. The treatment involves dipping a goose feather in rice vinegar to clear the phlegm from the throat, then using the goose feather to induce a cough, aiming to expel the purple blood from the worm for resolution; or grinding a purple gold ingot would also work. If it doesn't disperse, a small knife can be used to pierce and release the purple blood for recovery.

There is an ancient method to puncture the lesser shang point, which is very effective. Bloodletting with a knife or needle should be used in urgent cases, but there are also situations where it is not advisable. Xue refers to a case of a fifty-year-old man with a swollen and painful throat; when blood was drawn with a needle, his mind was clear, but his pulse was rapid and obscure, pressing it felt faint as if absent. It was said: "There is form but no pain, it resembles a yang condition, and thus one should strongly nourish the yin. But if one injures the yin blood, he is bound to perish." Subsequently, he indeed passed away. This case serves as a warning against careless use of blades or needles.

For throat wind conditions, the swelling penetrates outward, causing numbness, itching, and pain; in such cases, the antidote called xionghuang pills may be used.

An ancient method involves soaking paper in castor oil, twisting it into a wick, igniting it, then extinguishing it to create smoke that can be inhaled. Instantly, saliva will flow from the mouth and nose, and the jaw will relax, allowing for treatment directly at the afflicted area to ensure recovery.[67p]
For those with yang deficiency and throat pain, there are sores on the mouth and tongue, and symptoms worsen with exertion. The pulse will be floating and large, indicating deficiency of both spleen and lung qi, along with virtual heat in the bladder. One should use the Li Zhong Decoction, adding yam and shan zhu yu for recovery. For wind-heat in the upper jiao, use Jing Fang Bai Du San.

In cases of swollen and painful throat, with thirst and preference for cold drinks, along with constipation, all six pulses will be full. Purging will bring about recovery; one can use Fang Feng Tong Sheng San. There are many cases of virtual heat in the world, but few of actual heat. Such symptoms are rare, and this method should not be used lightly.

In cases of sudden throat blockage with a sound like snoring and phlegm that feels like being sawed, this indicates a lung crisis. It requires the urgent use of ginseng paste combined with ginger juice and bamboo juice taken openly. If the paste is not available, first boil ginseng decoction for rescue. Taking it early yields 70 to 80% results, next 40 to 50%, and if delayed, it cannot save.

Dan Xi states: for swollen and painful throats with yin deficiency and excessive yang energy, phlegm builds up above, the pulse will surely be floating and large. If pressure is applied, it will be weak; to save one from death is close, thus ginseng alone should be boiled thick and sipped slowly. Treating it as a solid condition invites disaster.

Zhong Jing says: for throat pain with heat in the Shao Yin, use 甘草汤 (Gancao Decoction). For cold and heat clashing in the Shao Yin, use 桔梗汤 (Jiegeng Decoction). For cold-induced throat pain in the Shao Yin, use a combination of Ban Xia San and decoction. For throat injuries causing sores which prevent speech, apply bitter wine soup.[68p]
For conditions of slight yin deficiency accompanied by guest heat, diarrhea, sore throat, fullness in the chest, and irritability, use Pigskin Decoction. People generally recognize heat associated with sore throats but are unaware of the existence of cold sore throats. The classics state: when the sun is at its zenith, cold dampness prevails, and people suffer from sore throats with swelling in the jaw. Chen Zangqi utilized prepared aconite peeled at the navel, sliced, and coated with honey, to allow the honey to penetrate the throat. The sweet taste diminishes, and it can be replaced. In the winter, cold accumulates in the kidney channel, leading to sore throats and diarrhea; aconite decoction warms the channel and thus provides relief.

Furthermore, during severe weather, if there are many cases of severe cold in the villages, it indicates violent exposure to cold, suppressing heat externally while trapping it internally. One must avoid using cold medicines like alum and sulfur to prevent further constricting yang energy. Also, avoid nitrate powder and other cold tonics, as these can push cold deep into the body, leading to serious consequences. Instead, one should use dispersing formulas, similar to Zhang Zhongjing's Sweet Tangerine Decoction.

There are also cases of yang toxin sore throats treated with Shengma Decoction, and yin toxin sore throats treated with Licorice Decoction. If medications for the sore throat prove ineffective, this is not actually a throat issue but pertains to a single red thread that appears in the nose like hair, with a black bubble the size of a cherry dangling to the throat's entrance, preventing the intake of food and drink. In this case, use a straight and solitary root of ox knee, clean it thoroughly, and mix three to five drops of quality vinegar. Grind finely and apply two or three drops into the nostrils. This will sever the thread and burst the bubble, bringing immediate relief.

Should there be persistent pain in the throat with chronic sores that refuse to heal, this is likely due to Yumberry ulcerative toxin, which should be primarily treated with Bi Xie Decoction.[69p]
Throat Closure Discussion

The throat is the passageway for qi; when it is open, it is beneficial, but when it is blocked, it causes harm, regardless of its primary or secondary causes. Therefore, it requires urgent treatment. Now, if we examine the various teachings of the ancients, and draw connections accordingly, we find the vital means for saving lives emerge clearly.

For emergencies involving severe throat closure, the prescription of Xiong Huang Jie Du Wan is advised. This condition directly relates to life and death; urgent treatment results in survival, whereas delayed treatment leads to death. The herbs in this formula—Xiong Huang can break down stagnant qi, Ba Dou helps expel thick phlegm, and Yu Jin disperses stagnant blood—can effectively address this closure.

For those with throat closure lasting several days that prevents eating, Xie Yan San can induce vomiting to clear phlegm, and once the phlegm is expelled, the illness is resolved. The sharp properties of Zao Jiao can break down stagnant qi, while the salty and bitter nature of Bai Fan can promote the release of thick phlegm; repeated expulsion will lead to the resolution of the illness.

For throat pain, Gan Ju Fang Feng Tang is recommended. The sweetness of Gan Cao mitigates urgent sensations in the throat; the bitterness of Jie Geng helps lower qi in the throat; the spiciness of Fang Feng can disperse blockage in the throat.

For throats affected by wind, applying Ba Dou oil on paper, twisting it into a strip, igniting it, and extinguishing it immediately after smoke rises allows the patient to open their mouth and apply the smoky end to the throat. After a moment, the expulsion of dark blood will alleviate the symptoms, and the patient can then eat porridge and drink. This approach, where heat from the fire reaches the Ba Dou oil, disperses blockages with the fire, flushes with Ba Dou, and expels through smoke, is a comprehensive strategy for effective relief.[70p]
External Medicine Authentic Text
By Chen Shigong (Ming Dynasty)

Discussion on Symptoms

It is asked: Sore throat pertains to the lungs, yet its causes are varied, with distinctions such as虚火 (empty fire) and实火 (full fire), tight throat and slow throat. Additionally, the throat is the gateway for the heart, lungs, liver, and kidneys for respiration, as well as the pathway for food, sound, and excretion. This connection affects the entire body and can be harmful quickly. Hence, it is said, "Look at the throat of a running horse," without delay.

In cases of empty fire, the color is pale with slight swelling, the pulse is thin and fine, urination is clear, and bowel movements are smooth. This is due to excessive thinking, insufficient central qi, and the spleen being unable to protect adequately, leading to easy ascent of empty fire. The discomfort first manifests as dryness in the throat, hindering food intake, causing coughs with phlegm, and difficulty in breathing, resulting in a coating that resembles moss, similar to shrimp skin, often irritating the throat. It feels like a hard object lodged in the throat, leading to vomiting of sour fluids and spitting out sweet saliva. In severe cases, there is a white coating on the tongue, pale lips, hoarseness of voice, and frequent coughing with phlegm.

All these symptoms arise from insufficient vitality of empty fire, and in treating this, one should not hastily use cooling medicines. For morning pain, it relates to qi deficiency, treated with Qi-invigorating decoction modified with Mai Dong, Wu Wei Zi, Niu Bang, and Yuan Shen. For afternoon pain, it relates to yin deficiency, treated with Four Substance Decoction modified with Huang Lian, Zhi Mu, Jie Geng, and Yuan Shen. If these do not prove effective, ginger should be added to guide the treatment, serving as an auxiliary method as well.[71p]
Real fire arises from excessive consumption of rich wine, indulging in fatty foods, piling up heavy bedding, and eating spicy and hot meals, leading to an accumulation of heat within. Over time, this stirs the fire and generates phlegm, resulting in a swollen throat. In severe cases, wind phlegm clogs it up, closing off the throat's entrance. Soon, fluids cannot enter, and the voice cannot be heard; this manifests as a tight throat and throat wind. If medication is ineffective, one should first use acupuncture to prick the throat, draining toxic blood. Then, applying tung oil with chicken feathers, one can induce the expulsion of thick phlegm, ensuring the phlegm and toxins are fully eliminated, allowing the throat entrance to relax so that soups and medicines can enter, and the voice can return.

For those who experience tightly clenched teeth that are hard to open, one must urgently pierce the minor seal to draw blood, which will cause the closure to open. If the needle probing does not expel phlegm and the voice sounds like a creaking saw while the nose lifts with phlegm and gasps, with fluids unable to enter and the voice silent, that indicates a true life-threatening condition.

There are also conditions such as throat carbuncles, throat paralysis, milk moth, and palatal abscesses. Although the afflicted may swell causing the throat entrance to be partially obstructed, the condition can still appear serious while the throat passage remains both wide and tight. These are all standard conditions, and although severe, they are manageable. One should use a golden key to expel phlegm and saliva, and administer a clearing broth to promote the release of accumulated heat. For pus swelling, it should be drained, what is damaged and painful should be nourished, leading to recovery.

In general, failing to let blood release for a closed throat, not eliminating phlegm for throat wind, not draining pus for throat carbuncles, and not needling or cauterizing for throat paralysis or milk moth are all improper practices. Furthermore, cases of phlegm fire causing coughs, which injure the throat, cannot be treated successfully.[72p]
The initial onset of red, swollen pain, with a clear voice and no simultaneous internal or external evidence, is mild. Once it has become swollen and painful, with the throat half open and half closed, and there is slight expectoration of phlegm, along with some intake of food, it is manageable. If the throat is swollen and closed, with a tight jaw, unclear speech, phlegm obstructing airflow, and a weak voice, it is dangerous. If the throat is suddenly closed, phlegm and saliva are obstructing, the mouth cannot open, and there is difficulty in breathing, it is fatal. Following sores, if toxicity accumulates in the throat leading to swelling, pain, and decay, making breathing unbearable and the voice hoarse, it is serious. Chronic cough due to phlegm heat, with deficiency of Yang rising, causing injury to the throat, results in hoarseness and a red face, which is also fatal.

Treatment methods:
For initial swelling and pain, with alternating cold and heat, along with dizziness and tightness, the evil is exterior and should be dispersed. If swelling and pain are accompanied by heat and a strong pulse with constipation, it indicates an internal evil and should be purged. For swelling and pain with cold and heat, dry mouth and intense thirst, and a large, strong pulse, it is advisable to both release the exterior and purge from within. When there is swelling and pain in the throat with significant phlegm obstruction, a flushed face and dry mouth indicate the evil is above, thus, it should be expelled. For a closed throat with phlegm, obstructing airflow and difficulty opening the mouth, first puncture the Shaoshang point and then proceed with expulsion. If there is already swelling and pain, with throat obstruction and inability to ingest liquids, and pus has formed, it requires urgent needling. If the swelling and pain are slightly red, with a weak pulse, and pain occurs in the afternoon, it indicates Yin deficiency and should nourish Yin and reduce fire; if the swelling and pain are white, with excessive expectoration in the morning, suggesting Yang deficiency, then the treatment should strengthen the spleen and tonify the middle.[73p]

Throat Abscess

The throat abscess arises outside the pharynx, with swelling and pain in the center, hindering eating and drinking, with redness, swelling, and heat, requiring drainage of pus. If it is soft and painful, needling is indicated; internally take tonifying medication, and apply jade-red ointment to help heal and close the mouth. In cases of internal erosion with fluids oozing from the hole, treatment has been effective for several individuals, and it is harmless.

Discussion

In ancient texts, the condition of throat obstruction is distinguished into eighteen types, all being categorized as "yang fire" by ancient scholars. However, although many of these patterns arise from fire, some do not originate from fire and must be examined closely. Fire can be true or false; true fire symptoms can be cleared, while false fire symptoms cannot be cleared and indicate water deficiency. Furthermore, there can be cases of excessive yin obstructing yang, indicating true cold symptoms. Therefore, the "Inner Canon" states: "The sun at the spring, cold dominance leads to pain in the throat and swelling of the jaw." This is precisely the meaning; why do later generations not investigate this? The throat obstruction involves various channels, including lesser yang, yangming, jueyin, and shaoyin, each with different manifestations of deficiency and excess.[74p]
The organs related to the Lesser Yang and Jueyin, being associated with wood and fire, indeed often manifest heat conditions. The Yangming, as the sea of food and water, allows the stomach qi to directly reach the throat, thus the fire of Yangming becomes the most abundant. To discern this, one only needs to observe that when emotional disturbances arise from frustration and anger, they mostly belong to the Lesser Yang and Jueyin, whereas those resulting from excessive consumption of rich, sweet, and spicy foods typically pertain to Yangming. For those suffering from this, it is generally appropriate to treat according to the principle of full fire.

As for the conditions related to the Lesser Yin, they are not comparable to these. The pulse of the Lesser Yin runs along the transverse bones, ending at the epiglottis, and is connected to the root of the tongue. When the Yin fire rises and causes a reverse flow upward, it often leads to throat obstruction. However, the fire of the Lesser Yin can either be empty or full and should not simply be classified as fire. If it indeed arises from full fire, there will be corresponding fire symptoms and clear pulse manifestations, which are also easy to identify. Conversely, if it is caused by excessive indulgence in alcohol and sexuality, leading to true Yin deficiency, this indicates a deficiency fire in the kidneys, and it cannot be supported by strong water.[75p]
There is a vacuous fire below that clashes with the Yang above; this is the fire without a root, namely the true cold condition in the kidneys, which cannot be treated without warming and supplementing the life gate. Although these various scriptures differ significantly, the differences between deficiency and excess are rarely understood by later generations. Only the "Chushi Yishu" discusses the examination of the upper conditions in relation to the lower, which indeed reflects the words of the Dao.

The conditions of the throat are generally referred to as fire; though there are many terms, some do not require precise distinction, yet there are others that must be differentiated. For instance, the single and double breast swellings and the throat wind are different. The swelling on both sides of the throat is called double breast swelling, while swelling on one side is called single breast swelling. Their shape must be round and protruding like a pearl, and they belong to the category of abscesses that form in the throat; therefore, they often release toxins and may require lancing to expel the blood for recovery.[76p]
If there is a wind that constricts the throat, the area will become red and swollen, not often purulent, and it need not bleed. Just reduce the heat, and the swelling will subside on its own. This is why the conditions differ, and there should be a proper method of treatment.

Pang said: The disease caused by repressed qi, in ancient texts, is referred to as kidney cold damage. This refers to those who have been suddenly exposed to intense cold, causing toxic qi to become trapped in the Shaoyin channel. Initially, there may be no illness, but after a period of ten days or months, symptoms may arise, with a faint pulse. The approach should be to treat it like cold damage, not as a throat blockage disease.

Next, there will likely be diarrhea. In my humble opinion, this symptom commonly occurs. It is necessary to utilize the fire of the Shaoyin and Shaoyang, along with the cold influence of the Taiyang and the dampness of the Taiyin, compounded with the evil of wind and cold, all of which can bring about this condition. Therefore, when treating this, there’s no need to specifically address the throat blockage; instead, focus on expelling the external evil, and the throat will heal on its own. For instance, many formulas containing Chai Hu and various scattered methods can be adjusted accordingly for use.[77p]

On Treatment

For fire-related throat obstruction, it is best to focus on drinking a decoction aimed at resolving it; if the fire is not severe, a shift in the decoction can help. When there is excess liver and gallbladder fire, the main ingredients should be peony, gardenia, and gentian. For excess stomach fire, gypsum should be the primary ingredient. If there is severe constipation, larger doses of rhubarb and Glauber's salt should be added to relieve the bowel and reduce the fire naturally. If the fire rises to the upper body and causes heat to accumulate in the head, face, and throat, it is crucial to clear and descend it; never use remedies to disperse wind or raise yang, as this will only cause the fire to further flare up from within. As the classics state, "Suppress the high," which refers directly to this situation; it does not mean that obstructed fire should be released or that raising yang is needed. Scholars must discern this clearly and not mistake its essence.

Regarding external treatment for fire-related swelling and pain, it is best to grind the seeds of the bitter cucumber with vinegar, then use a goose quill to swab the throat to remove phlegm; alternatively, dilute it with some water to avoid excessive acidity, and periodically gargle without swallowing, expelling phlegm for better results. After gargling, use a spoon to blow the decoction, and still take the herbal medicine internally for guaranteed recovery. If the fire is trapped above, food remedies like snow pear juice or mung bean drinks are ideal. In regions where pears are scarce, good radish juice can be pounded and mixed with spring water, adding a little starch to blend it, and sipped slowly; this will both eliminate phlegm and clear heat.

For cases involving single or double moth larvae, if the toxicity is mild and there is no formation of pus, treatment can help disperse it; if the condition is severe and critical, it is essential to perform bloodletting to hasten recovery.[78p]
This is due to urgency and thus cannot be helped but must be used. Furthermore, in ancient practices, using a three-edged needle to puncture the Shaoshang point to induce bleeding is said to treat throat obstruction and achieve immediate relief.

For throat obstruction due to Yin deficiency, symptoms include internal heat, thirst, dryness of the throat, and possibly red lips and flushed cheeks, with phlegm and saliva accumulating. However, the pulse must be weak, and although the six pulses may be rapid, they feel floating and soft with no strength. One should observe if there has been excessive indulgence in alcohol or erotic desires, or if the individual is naturally deficient in Yin energy, experiencing fatigue and weakness. This indicates a deficiency in kidney Yin, where water fails to restrain fire. When fire is severe, it is advised to use the Eight Ingredients Decoction for nourishing Yin, or modifications of the One Yin Decoction. If there is mild fire, a dislike for cold substances, soft stools, and urine that is not hot, then the Six-Ingredient Rehmannia Decoction or similar preparations should be applied. If caused by excessive worry and mental strain alongside active heart fire, the Two Yin Decoction should be used.

For throat obstruction due to Yang inversion, if the fire does not return to its source, the fire becomes a guest in the throat, leading to symptoms of heat above and cold below, distinctly different from typical fire patterns. In such cases, one should only find the six pulses weak, without a slippery or strong indication; moreover, there are no fire symptoms in the lower body and the abdomen dislikes cold. These signs typically arise from indulgence in lust harming essence, excessive diarrhea damaging the kidneys, or the absence of real fire combined with excessive consumption of cold substances which harms Yang energy. For this condition, urgent use of the Tranquil Yin Decoction is recommended, followed by the Eight-Ingredient Rehmannia Decoction; alternatively, dissolving honey with Aconite in the mouth is also effective. If further cold is employed, it will certainly lead to dire consequences.

Throat obstruction due to Yang deficiency does not arise from a throat issue caused by Yang deficiency; rather, it is throat obstruction stemming from pre-existing Yang deficiency.[79p]
There are those whose throat ailments are caused by excessive aggression, resulting in harm to the stomach's energy; some struggle with food and drink, leading to empty storerooms, which also harms the stomach's energy; and there are others whose energy is inherently weak, and who cannot withstand fatigue, causing harm to the stomach's energy. Generally, when there is inner deficiency of middle energy and external pressure causing pain, it often results in the departure of original yang, with a floating and scattered pulse, or a weak and thin pulse, leading to a snoring-like sound and sputum as if being cut with a saw. This indicates a severe depletion of the lungs and stomach, and one should promptly restore the original energy by simmering ginseng alone, and sip it slowly with peace of mind; if there is excessive phlegm, bamboo juice or ginger juice may be added. If the remedy is delayed, there may be dire consequences; treating it with approaches for excess heat will bring disaster as quickly as a snap of the fingers.

For throat ulcer conditions, those who are generally weakened from yin deficiency often suffer from this illness; the symptoms include swollen and ulcerated throats that fail to heal over long periods. This is a case of substantial water deficiency and latent fire, and should be treated using methods for yin deficiency and throat ailments. If there is frequent coughing due to lung heat, the treatment should involve preparations like Si Yin Decoction. In cases where there are ulcers in the throat that are painful and broken, it is advisable to use Niuhuang Yijing Powder for blowing and applying, while also internally taking nourishing agents for true yin to facilitate complete recovery.

Plague-induced throat ailments arise from the atmospheric plague's influence, presenting with throat pain and swelling of the neck, particularly severe swelling of the head and face, especially in the northern regions. This illness is commonly referred to as "toad plague" among the people, or also called "cormorant plague" and "big head plague." This condition, characterized by extreme dampness and heat, is most dangerous, and one should clear the accumulated heat from all meridians, or drain the heat of the Yangming channel, taking care to assess urgency in treatment. Dongyuan has a remedy called Pujixiaodong Decoction, specifically for treating plague-related throat ailments, which is highly effective.[80p]
The condition known as "Locked Throat Wind" is often identified by symptoms such as swelling and pain in the throat, difficulty in eating and drinking, or phlegm and gas obstructing the passage, all of which are referred to as "Locked Throat Wind." However, what truly constitutes Locked Throat Wind is exceedingly strange and urgent, and little is known about it.

While in Yandu, I once encountered a girl who had reached the age of maturity. One day in mid-autumn, she suddenly developed a tight and constricted throat without any preceding illness, and her breathing became labored. Within half a day, her condition worsened significantly. When I was called to treat her, I examined her pulse and found no sign of heat. When I asked about her throat, there was neither swelling nor pain. Observing her appearance, her face was pale and her eyes wide, unable to speak. Listening to her voice, it was as delicate as a needle, and her attempts to breathe were desperate like a thread; she strained her neck as if fighting for her life, in a state of pitiable distress. I was left in doubt, unable to comprehend the situation.[81p]
The intention is to indicate that the wind pathogen obstructs the throat passages; it cannot be resolved without using pungent and warming herbs. Thus, I added fresh ginger to Erchen Decoction, brewed it, and administered it, but there was no effect at all. I intended to use Dushen Decoction to save the lungs; however, seeing the condition so dire, I feared it would stir grievances and slander, and I ultimately did not dare to take action. Other physicians, upon seeing this, could only stand by without taking any measures. In this way, one person passed away after a day and night. Subsequently, another person met the same fate. As for these two individuals, I still do not understand the cause of their illness, which remains a lifelong perplexity, and I feel deeply ashamed. Nevertheless, it must be that the lung qi was completely exhausted. If another case arises, I fear that Dushen Decoction alone cannot provide salvation. Therefore, I record this here, hoping that future gentlemen will take it to heart and consider it carefully.

When there is poison from the Yangmei fruit causing ulceration and pain in the throat that does not heal after a long time, this is not a case of throat blockage, but rather a Yangmei sore toxin. One should use Xianyi Liang Decoction; in severe cases, prepare a decoction of earth Poria and swallow Wubao Pill.

Shishis Secret Manuscript 【Qing Dynasty, Chen Shiduo】[82p]

Swelling and Pain

When a person has a throat condition with significant swelling, which is neither a goiter nor a tumor, the pain may come and go. Externally, there are colorful patterns visible, and when pressed, it feels both empty and solid. This is due to phlegm disease that manifests like a tumor but is neither truly one nor a goiter. The prescription consists of 9 grams each of seaweed, banxia (Pinellia), white mustard seed, fritillaria, ginseng, platycodon (bellflower), and nanking (south stars), 15 grams of poria, 3 grams each of kelp and licorice, and 0.3 grams of aconite, decocted in water for oral administration. This formula is a miraculous medicine to dissolve phlegm in the upper burner. Seaweed and kelp help remove external signs of the goiter and eliminate the strange colorful patterns. The key is to resolve phlegm without damaging qi, thereby keeping the stomach qi strong and facilitating the transformation of phlegm. With one dose, one knows; two doses can eliminate most of it; three doses can completely dissolve it; and four doses will prevent recurrence. This formula can also treat goiter symptoms and is remarkably effective.

If a person suddenly has swelling and pain in the throat, accompanied by double eyelids, such that they cannot eat, they could die within five days without food. However, this condition of real fire is easier to treat. For real fire, one can use mountain bean root, and herbs like qin (skullcap), lian (lotus), banxia, chaihu (bupleurum), licorice, platycodon, and tianhuafeng (trichosanthes) for immediate relief. Yet, the condition of false fire occurs when kidney fire does not settle in the mingmen (life gate) but floats between the throat. Its symptoms resemble those of real fire, but are heavier at night and lighter in the morning. Conversely, with real fire, symptoms are heavier in the morning and lighter at night. Real fire causes dryness and cracking in the mouth; false fire does not create much thirst but shows a slippery tongue without cracks. Use this method of distinguishing symptoms to avoid mistakes.[83p]
These虚痛s (false pains), if treated with methods meant for real fire, are like a person who has fallen into a well and then adds stones to it. Therefore, not only should one avoid cold and cooling treatments, but one should also refrain from using dispersing methods, as虚火 (false fire) must be supplemented. However, merely supplementing kidney water, while water can control fire, may only alleviate the situation slightly, as the fire is too intense and hard to subdue. It is better to supplement fire with water, leading the fire back to its original source, causing its force to vanish in an instant. One should use the Y引火 Decoction: prepared Rehmannia and Fritillaria (each 1 tael), white mustard seed (3 qian), Chinese dogwood and yam (each 4 qian), northern spices and cinnamon (each 2 qian), poria (5 qian), then decoct with water and take as a dose, which will calm the phlegm, relieve the pain, and eliminate the swelling; two doses will bring complete recovery. The prepared Rehmannia, Chinese dogwood, and spices primarily reinforce kidney water; poria and yam also benefit essence and facilitate water, assisting the descent of cinnamon; Fritillaria dissipates the floating fire above; while white mustard seeds eliminate obstructive phlegm. Once the upper focus is relaxed and the lower focus receives the warmth of cinnamon, is there any chance that the fire of the dragon and thunder will not return to its root in the mingmen? One dose is effective. The unpredictable workings of spirits and ghosts are even better than the Eight-Flavored Rehmannia Decoction. If the throat is swollen and blocked, and not even a spoonful of water can be swallowed, how will this formula be applied? Furthermore, there is another method: use one piece of aconite, five qian of broken old paper, ground into powder, mix into a paste, shape it into a patch as large as a teacup, apply it to the center of the sole, and warm it with fire for a while. After one period, the throat will widen, opening a pathway to take medicine.[84p]
Moth of Milk

There are some who suffer from a dual moth condition, which others mistakenly attribute to heat. The throat swells painfully, phlegm incessantly thick like sawdust, and not a single drop of tea can be swallowed. Isn’t this a sign of heat? Yet, despite the intense pain, it becomes somewhat lighter by morning; although the throat is swollen, the tongue will not be dry; although there is abundant phlegm, it will not be yellow and clotted. This is a sign of false heat. If one hastily uses cold and cool medicines for urgent relief, it may seem to soothe the throat momentarily, but soon the heat intensifies even more. People assume that the cooling medicine was insufficient and add more cold remedies, which only aggravates the condition. It is urgent to prick the Shaoshang point to draw a little blood; this will surely open a line of passage in the throat. It is essential to use one qian of Aconite, one liang of Rehmannia, four qian of Cornus, three qian each of Ophiopogon, Chinese Amomum, and Achyranthes, and five qian of Poria; decoct and administer down the throat, and a sound shall resonate, causing the fiery heat to dissipate immediately.[85p]
The fire of the Lesser Yin is like a galloping horse. When a person loses a significant amount of kidney water, the original Yang in the kidneys cannot settle down, as there is no water to nourish the fire, which must then rise. Daily, it surges upward and constricts the throat, making it unable to properly function, leading to swellings and pains resembling double moths, though they are not actually double moths. The key lies in using spicy and warm drugs like aconite to guide the fire of the dragon and thunder down into the dwelling. The fire of the dragon and thunder represents the fire of the heart; it enjoys water but dislikes fire. Therefore, herbs like cooked rehmannia and shan zhu yu, which are purely nourishing for Yin, are used to give the fire a place to return, preventing it from boiling over. This is due to counteracting its reverse tendencies. What it enjoys is the true Yin water, not the cold and cooling type; what it dislikes is the fire of邪气 (xieqi), not the spicy and warm fire. As for the condition of having heavier days and lighter nights, it is the easiest to treat.[86p]
Using three qian of mountain bean root and balloon flower, and one qian each of pinellia and licorice, a single dose will cure immediately, provided it is not a case of reverse syndrome. For the symptoms of dual moths with yin deficiency, there are additional methods of treatment. Use one qian of aconite, fried with salt water into pieces; hold one piece in the mouth to immediately enable the use of decoction. Then, take one liang of Eight Flavor Pill with boiling water, and it can also cure immediately.

Moreover, the yin syndrome of dual moths is both the most difficult and the easiest to treat. Not knowing the key makes it very hard, but knowing the method makes it very easy. I often treat this illness using one piece of aconite, with one he of salt, boiled in water until thoroughly cooked, allowing the patient to hold one piece in the mouth, after which the fire will stop; then, take a large dose of Six Flavor Decoction, and it will not recur—this is a divine formula.[87p]
The condition of the "yin moth" is due to a deficiency of kidney water, where the fire cannot be contained below and thus rises above. The throat is narrow, preventing the fire from being released directly, resulting in the formation of a "moth," which resembles a moth but is not. The pain is lighter in the morning and heavier in the afternoon, exacerbating by dusk. It is relieved by heat and worsened by coolness. In severe cases, even a drop of water cannot go down the throat. If treated as an external wind-heat condition using herbs like mountain soy root, qin (scutellaria), lian (lotus), and gardenia, the pain may increase and the throat will remain obstructed, potentially leading to death. Only by nourishing the yin deficiency and employing methods that redirect fire to its source can the pain be alleviated. This is known as the "Transforming Moth Pill," consisting of one liang each of reheated land (shudihuang), shanzhu yu (cornelian cherry), and mai dong (ophiopogon), along with 1 qian of fu zi (prepared aconite) and 3 qians of che qian zi (plantago) and 2 qians of bei wu wei zi (schisandra). These ingredients are decocted in water for ingestion. This formula greatly nourishes the kidney water, rather than treating the pain of the "moth." Strengthening the water will quell the fire; thus, the pain dissipates, making this method exceptionally effective.[88p]
Throat Gateway

Prescription

Jingfang Baidu Powder
Jing Jie Suan, Fang Feng, Qiang Huo, Du Huo, Chai Hu, Qian Hu, Chuan Xiong, Zhi Ke, Jie Geng, Fu Ling, each one tael; Gan Cao five qian. Take one tael each time, add three slices of fresh ginger and a little mint, and decoct.

Qing Yan Li Ge Decoction
For treating accumulated heat causing swollen and painful throat, with phlegm and saliva congestion. Jin Yin Hua, Fang Feng, Jing Jie, Mint, Jie Geng, Huang Qin (stir-fried), Huang Lian (stir-fried), half a qian each; Shan Zhi, Lian Qiao, two qian each; Yuan Shen, Da Huang (stewed), (Shi Bu) Nitrate, Niu Bang Zi (burdock seeds) ground, Gan Cao, each seven fen. Prepare a dose with two sheng of water, decoct to one sheng, and take after meals. Removing Jin Yin Hua from this formula yields the Qing Xin Li Ge Decoction, treating the same condition.

Golden Key
For treating closed throat with excess phlegm and saliva, making it hard to swallow liquids. Combine half a sheng of fire nitrate, five qian of borax, a character of brain powder, two qian of realgar, and one qian of white silkworm, each ground separately and mixed. Blow the mixture onto the affected area with a bamboo tube; phlegm and saliva will be expelled. If phlegm is expelled but the throat remains blocked, needle the affected area to remove bad blood.[89p]
Liangge San: Treats throat obstruction.
Ingredients: Huangqin (scutellaria), wine-fried; Zhizi (gardenia), fried; Bohe (mint), each one liang; Lianqiao (forsythia), four liang; Dahuang (rhubarb), soaked in wine; Mangxiao (mirabilite), Gancao (licorice), each two liang. Grind together into a powder; take five qian each time.

Fangfeng Tongsheng San: Treats throat obstruction and throat abscess.
Ingredients: Fangfeng (siler), Chuanxiong (ligusticum), Danggui (angelica), Baishao (white peony), Dahuang (rhubarb), raw; Mangxiao (mirabilite), Lianqiao (forsythia), Bohe (mint), Mahuang (ephedra), Baizhu (attractylodes), Zhizi (gardenia), fried and black; Jingjie (schizonepeta), each five qian; Shigao (gypsum), Jiegeng (platycodon), Huangqin (scutellaria), each one liang; Huashi (talc), three liang; Gancao (licorice), two liang. Grind together into a powder; take two qian each time, with one cup of water, three slices of ginger, boil down to six fen, and take warm.

Buzhong Yiqi Tang: Treats the aforementioned conditions that belong to qi deficiency.
Ingredients: Huangqi (astragalus), one qian and five fen; Renshen (ginseng), Gancao (licorice), each one qian; Baizhu (attractylodes), Danggui (angelica), Chenpi (dried tangerine peel), Chaihu (bupleurum), each five fen; Shengma (cimicifuga), three fen. Decoction with ginger and jujube water.

Sishen Tang: Treats the aforementioned conditions that belong to blood deficiency.
Ingredients: Danggui (angelica), washed with wine; Shudi (reheated rehmannia), each three qian; Chuanxiong (ligusticum), washed with wine, one qian and five fen; Baishao (white peony), fried with wine, two qian. Decoction with water; take warm.

Poguan San: Treats throat obstruction and throat abscess.
Ingredients: Dahuang (rhubarb), two liang, half raw and half cooked; Mangxiao (mirabilite), Gancao (licorice), each one liang. Grind together into a powder, refine with honey into small balls the size of a marble; take half a ball each time, washed down with warm tea or wine after meals. Half a cup of urine of a child, ground and taken as well. Avoid cold water.[90p]
Qing Wei San treats damp-heat in the stomach channel, swelling and pain in the teeth and throat, which may pull on the head or cause facial heat, and it addresses these issues.
Mix one qian of Angelica Sinensis with wine; two qian each of Coptis Chinensis and raw Rehmannia with wine; one and a half qian of Peony Root; and two fen of Cimicifuga.
Prepare one dose with two zhongs of water, decoct until reduced to seven points, and take it away from meals.

Jing Jie Decoction is for treating swelling and pain in the throat, inability to speak, and severe pain when swallowing.
Use half a liang of Jing Jie, two liang of Platycodon, and one liang of Licorice.
Grind the above into powder, take four qian with one cup of water, add three slices of ginger, decoct until reduced to six points, then strain and take warm.

Bi Xue is used for all kinds of accumulated heat, sores on the mouth and tongue, irritability and throat constriction, and pain in the teeth and gums.
Use two liang each of Glauber's Salt, Indigo, calcined Cold Water Stone, calcined Gypsum, along with two liang each of Sodium Carbonate, Manganese Carbonate, Licorice, and Talc.
Prepare a decoction of Licorice with two sheng of water, add the other herbs and decoct again, stirring continuously with a willow branch until melted. Pour into a sand basin and let it cool to form frost, then grind the frost into a powder. Use a small amount to dissolve and swallow. If the throat is constricted to the point of inability to swallow, use a bamboo tube to blow the medicine into the throat.

Po Guan Dan treats the closure of the throat due to phlegm, throat constriction, and related symptoms.
Use five qian of Borax powder and one liang of Frosted Plum Meat, mix and crush finely.[91p]
The two ingredients on the right are to be mixed and formed into pills the size of chestnuts. Each dosage consists of one pill to be dissolved in the mouth and swallowed. Internally, take Jingfang Baiduxian powder.

Banxia Guizhi Gancao Decoction is used to treat sore throat due to sudden cold. Ingredients include 2.5 qian each of Banxia, Guizhi, and Gancao, along with 2 bowls of water and 5 slices of fresh ginger. Boil until reduced to 80% of the original volume, strain, and gradually sip.

Jiedu Xionghuang Pill treats pharyngeal wind and acute pharyngitis, sudden collapse, teeth clenched, and loss of consciousness. Prepare 1 liang each of powdered Xionghuang and Yujin, and 14 peeled processed Ba Dou. Mix into a fine powder, boil with vinegar, then form into small pills like mung beans. Take 7 pills with hot tea to expel stubborn phlegm, leading to immediate recovery. If the patient does not expel, administer another dose. If the patient is near death but still has warmth in the heart, if medicines cannot be swallowed, then use a knife and iron spoon to open the mouth for administration; they will not fail to revive. For children with convulsions and phlegm obstructing the throat, adjust the dosage to 2 to 3 pills based on size. One method involves taking 3 grains of Xionghuang Pill, dissolved in vinegar, is especially effective, as phlegm will immediately be expelled.

Xiaoxuming Decoction treats throat obstruction and throat abscess. Ingredients include Ma Huang (dried and cut), Ren Shen, roasted Huangqin, roasted Bai Shao, washed Chuan Xiong, Fang Ji, and peeled, roasted Apricot kernels (double kernels), each at 1 qian; and Fang Feng and peeled, roasted Fu Zi, each at 0.5 qian. Boil the above ingredients in water for internal consumption.[92p]

Fangfeng San treats swollen and painful throats. Use less for those with deficiency and more for those with excess. The ingredients are: Fangfeng (siler), ginger, stir-fried silkworms, honeysuckle, borax, schizonpeta, Huangyaozi, rhubarb wrapped in moist paper and baked until fragrant, Xixin (asarum), Chuanxiong, red internal dissolvent, mountain bean root, turmeric, and licorice, each half an ounce, with three qian of Yaxiao (a type of salt) and half a jin of mint. Zhuifeng San treats swollen and painful throats. The ingredients are: yellow sulfur, salted niter, calcined soapberry pods, and calcined cardamom shells, each half an ounce. If there are ulcers in the throat with pain, use steamed pig brain mixed with light ginger vinegar to eat, and it will be effective.

Kaiguan San treats blockages caused by wind in the throat. The ingredients are: white silkworms, fried and with the silk removed, and dried white alum in equal parts. Seven Treasures Powder: For treating throat constriction and wind constricting the throat.

Melon Stem Powder: For treating wind constricting the throat, causing a sensation of binding air in the throat.
The quantity of melon stems is not fixed. Grind the melon stems finely into powder; adults take one character, and those over fifteen or elderly take half a character. In the morning, mix with well water and take with a piece of sugar to hold in the mouth; after a long time, saliva will flow like water. For those who have deepened conditions, if the saliva diminishes, there will be a piece like stone; if it is floated or looks like a mirror on water, when the saliva is gone, eat congee for one or two days. This medicine does not cause severe vomiting, only the expulsion of saliva. Furthermore, the melon stems must be harvested naturally; those that have fallen are to be used without utilizing them. Wrap them in betel palm leaves and hang them to dry in a windy area against the east wall.[95p]
Wu Xi Gao: Treats swollen and painful throats, including all forms of throat obstruction and ulceration, such as hidden corpse, throat binding, throat numbness, urgent throat issues, flying threads entering the throat, heavy tongue, wooden tongue, and similar conditions.

Take two pieces of soapberry, crush them, soak in three sheng (a volume measure) of water for one period, repeatedly knead to extract the juice and discard the residue, then place into a pottery vessel and boil down to a paste. Add one cup of good wine, a pinch of saltpeter, and one qian each of powdered herb frost, mix well to thicken, along with one qian of powdered ginseng. Add a small amount of borax and white plum frost, and grind into the paste.

Combine the preceding ingredients, use a goose feather to apply a small amount to the throat until the stubborn phlegm is expelled, then chew two inches of licorice, swallow the juice and saliva.

Bei Ji Ru Sheng San: Treats seasonal throat wind afflictions, gradually obstructing the throat and preventing food and water from going down, with tightly clenched teeth and loss of consciousness.

Yi Zi San: Treats throat closure, air blockage, and inability to ingest food and drink.
