Dried Ginger Powder
Treats hanging sores that suddenly swell and heat up.
Dried ginger and half summer (Ban Xia) are washed to remove the slickness, equally divided.
Grind these into a fine powder and place a small amount on the tongue to swallow.

Yuan Shen Powder
Treats hanging sores accompanied by pain and loss of appetite.
Equal parts of Sheng Ma, She Gan, and Da Huang (each half a tael), with two and a half qian of Gan Cao and one tael of Yuan Shen.
Grind into a fine powder, decoct in water until reduced to seven parts, let cool, and hold in the mouth to swallow. It is very effective.

She Gan Pills
Treats swelling and pain of hanging sores and difficulty in the throat.
Wash apricot seeds, removing skins, tips, and double seeds, then lightly roast with bran until slightly yellow, and combine with equal parts of roasted Gan Cao and She Gan.
Also, lightly stir-fry Sheng Ma and Da Huang, and half a qian each of Mu Bie Zi.
Grind these into a fine powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of a ball, and often keep one in the mouth to swallow.

Salt and Alum Powder
Treats hanging sore in the throat that is long and obstructive, causing a feeling of heaviness.
Burn salt and dry white alum.
Grind finely, mix in equal parts. Apply with the tip of a chopstick and it will dissolve.

She Gan Pills
Treats swelling and pain of hanging sores, difficulty in the throat, and heat in the chest.
One tael each of She Gan, Tian Zhu Huang (Pomegranate Yellow), and Ma Ya Xie (Horse Tooth Nitre), along with half a tael each of rhino horn shavings, Yuan Shen, Chuan Sheng Ma, roasted Gan Cao, Bai Yao, Huang Yao, and white alum.
Grind into a fine powder, mix well, and use honey to bind and pound into pills the size of small balls. There is no specific time for use; wrap one in cotton and keep in the mouth to swallow.[102p]
Borosilicate powder, for treating swelling and pain of hanging sores.

Grind two qian each of borosilicate, Ma Ya salt, talcum powder, and cold water stone; grind half a qian of powdered brain; one and a half qian of white alum. This mixture should be made into a fine powder. Each use is half a qian, taken at any time with fresh spring water.

Qi Guan powder, for treating wind-heat invading the upper burner, causing swelling and pain from hanging sores.

Roast two liang of bitter herbs and use fresh licorice. This should also be made into a fine powder. Each dose is two qian, used with one cup of water, decocted for six minutes, then swish in the mouth for a long time before swallowing.

Huang Qi powder, for treating throat sores and pain.

Half a liang each of Huang Qi, betel nut, purple aster (washed), burdock seed, gardenia seed, red poria, and fresh licorice; three qian each of Cimicifuga and Scutellaria; one liang each of Yuanshen and Ophiopogon. Grind finely. Each dose is one qian with one cup of water, decocted down to six minutes, then strain and take.

Tao Hong powder, for treating sores and swelling in the throat, presenting red-purple coloration, causing pain that hinders swallowing.

Ten pieces each of gold and silver foil, a little lead white frost, four liang of cold water stone, and two liang of Taiyin original essence stone. These two ingredients should be crushed, placed into a container, fired until they turn red, then buried in the ground to release heat toxins, and ground finely.

Grind one liang each of Ma Ya salt, cinnabar, and roasted licorice into a fine powder. Each dose is one character's worth mixed with licorice water; alternatively, make small pills the size of peas using thin glutinous rice porridge, hold in the mouth to dissolve and swallow.[103p]
Amber and rhinoceros horn ointment treats sores in the throat, mouth, and tongue caused by pathogens. Genuine amber is ground with rhinoceros horn shavings, each one qian, along with raw ginseng (with the husk removed), sour jujube seeds (with the husk removed), and cultivable red cinnabar, each two qian. Grind these into a fine powder, mix thoroughly, and refine with honey to make an ointment, stored in ceramic containers. When symptoms arise, take one bolus, using tianmen dong (asparagus) without the heart, and brew it strongly to dissolve. Take five doses in one day.

Life-saving powder treats heat toxins in the spleen and stomach that ascend and cause sores in the throat, along with phlegm in the throat. Use three qian of greasy powder, two and a half qian of cinquefoil, chopped rhubarb (stir-fried), yellow root, and white silkworms (stir-fried), each half a liang of raw licorice. Grind these into a fine powder; take one bolt each time. Adults can inhale it through a bamboo tube, while children can blow it through a bamboo tube. If the residual toxins attack the heart, and there are sores in the lungs and throat, use a boy's breast milk to adjust the medicine taken with a chicken feather. Vomiting means survival; if not vomiting, the outcome is death.[104p]
Burdock Seed Pills: Treats sores and swelling in the throat caused by heat and toxins. Use one ounce of burdock seeds, lightly roasted; half an ounce each of angelica, yellow medicine, dried duckweed, root of Scrophularia, and raw licorice. Grind all to a fine powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of a marble, and orally dissolve one pill to swallow saliva regularly.

Borax Powder: Treats sores and swelling in the throat caused by wind-heat affecting the heart and spleen, which may lead to swelling of the tongue or thickened tongue with obstruction preventing liquid intake. Grind three ounces of borax; one ounce each of mint leaves and cattail pollen; half an ounce each of indigo, plantain, Scrophularia, poria, sand, talc, and Schizonepeta spikes; half an ounce each of mountain bean root and raw licorice. Prepare two and a half ounces of calcined cold water stone; mix all into a fine powder. Take half a penny’s worth at any time, dissolved in freshly drawn water.

Banxia Houpu Decoction, also known as Enhanced Four-Seven Decoction, treats preceding symptoms. Ingredients: one penny each of perilla leaves, pinellia, magnolia bark, red poria, dried tangerine peel, bitter orange fruit, south star, sand; seven-tenths of a penny of green peel; three-tenths each of betel nut and amomum; six-tenths of a penny of white cardamom; five slices of ginger. Boil with water for consumption.[105p]
Shegan San: Treats the sensation of something obstructing the throat, causing discomfort, choking, and pain, making swallowing difficult. Ingredients: Shegan, Jiegeng, Chuan Shengma, rhino horn powder—each 9 grams; Muxiang, Mutong—each 15 grams; Zisuzi (stir-fried), He Li Le (pitted), Betel nut, Zhike (husks removed and stir-fried), Chiffonized Polyporus (Fu Ling), and honey-roasted licorice—each 30 grams. Grind to a fine powder. For each dose, take 9 grams, mix with one cup of water, and simmer until reduced to 80%. Strain and take warm at any time.

Long Nao Wan: Treats the sensation of a round object in the throat, causing difficulty in swallowing saliva, thirst, and pain. It requires deep needling of swollen areas to dispel toxic qi. Ingredients: Long Nao (dragon brain), musk—each 7.5 grams; Congruent essential powder, Ma Ya Xiao, Sheng Ma, Huang Qi—each 30 grams; stir-fried Dahuang and honey-roasted licorice—each 15 grams; Sheng Di Huang—250 grams, extract the juice and mix with the medicine. Grind into a fine powder, mix well, and use the Di Huang juice to form pills the size of pellets. Take as needed, wrapped in cotton to dissolve in saliva to promote throat comfort.

Muxiang San: Treats the sensation of something obstructing the throat, making swallowing impossible and expulsion difficult. Ingredients: Muxiang—15 grams; Zixue, Shegan, Antelope horn powder, rhino horn powder, Betel nut—each 30 grams; Yuanshen, Sangbai Pi, Sheng Ma—each 45 grams. Grind finely; for each dose, take 9 grams, mix with one cup of water, simmer until reduced to 60%. Strain and take warm at any time.[106p]
Luo Shi Decoction: Treats the sensation of an obstructive mass in the throat.
Luo Shi and Zi Wan, each half a tael; Sheng Ma and She Gan, each seven and a half qian; Mu Tong, Chi Fu Ling, and Jie Geng, stir-fried, each one tael. Pound all and finely grind. Take five qian with a ladle of water, decoct until reduced to eight portions, strain, and take warm after meals. If needed for unblocking, add one qian of Mangxiao powder to the decoction, mix well and consume. Luo Shi refers to Shi Bei Li.

Si Wei Decoction: Treats sensation of obstruction in the throat, with difficulty swallowing and spitting.
Ban Xia soaked overnight in ginger juice, then washed and sliced; Hou Po scraped to remove the coarse skin, soaked in ginger juice and roasted until yellow; Chen Pi soaked in broth to remove the white part and then toasted, all one tael. Chi Fu Ling, scraped to remove black skin, two taels. Pound all and finely grind. Take three qian with a ladle of water, add one large piece of ginger and a jujube, broken, decoct until reduced to six portions, strain, and take warm before meals.

Apricot Kernel Decoction Pills: Treats obstruction in the throat where food cannot go down, as if there is a mass stuck.
Apricot kernels soaked in decoction, with the skin tip and double kernels removed, roasted, half a tael; Guan Gui with coarse skin removed; Loquat leaves wiped clean of fuzz, roasted; Ren Shen each one tael. Grind all into a fine powder, combine with honey to make pills the size of cherries. Take one pill, hold in the mouth to dissolve and swallow saliva, adjusting based on recovery.[107p]
Gancao Xiexin Decoction: Treats the previous symptoms. Ingredients: Huangqin, Renshen, Ganjiang, each 3 taels; 12 Da Zao, split; Banxia, 0.5 sheng; Gancao, 4 taels; Huanglian, 1 tael. Combine these seven ingredients with 10 dou of water, boil to extract 6 sheng, then remove the residue, reboil, and take 1 sheng warm, three times a day.

Kushen Decoction: Treats Huohuo disease; parasites in the lower body cause dryness in the throat. Ingredients: Kushen, 0.5 jin; Huai Baipi, Wolf's Tooth Root, each 4 taels. Grind these, add 5 sheng of water, boil down to 3.5 sheng, and wash the lower body.

Xiaojianzhong Decoction: Treats the previous symptoms. Ingredients: Guizhi, Zhizhi Gancao, each 3 taels; 12 Da Zao; Shaoyao, 6 taels; Shengjiang, 3 taels; Jiao Yi, 1 sheng. Combine these six ingredients with 7 sheng of water, boil the first five ingredients, take 3 sheng, remove the residue, add Jiao Yi, and simmer gently to dissolve. Take 1 sheng warm, three times a day.

Shegan Mahuang Decoction: Treats the previous symptoms. Ingredients: Shegan, 13 pieces; Mahuang, 4 taels; Shengjiang, 4 taels; Xixin, Zihuan, and Donghua, each 3 taels; Wuweizi, 0.5 sheng; large Banxia, wash and use 8 pieces; 7 Da Zao. Combine these nine ingredients with 12.2 dou of water, first boil Mahuang, remove the foam, add the other herbs, and boil to get 3 sheng. Divide into three warm doses. Some sources suggest using 3 taels of Shegan and 0.5 sheng of Banxia.[108p]
Shengma Bie Jia Decoction, also known as Shu Jiao Decoction, treats the above-mentioned conditions.

  • Ingredients:
    • 1 tael of Dang Gui,
    • 2 taels each of Sheng Ma and Gan Cao (Licorice),
    • One piece of Bie Jia the size of a finger, roasted,
    • 0.5 tael of Xiong Huang (Realgar), ground.

Mix these six ingredients with 4 sheng of water, boil down to 1 sheng, and take as a single dose; elders and children should take it again to induce sweating.

Mai Men Dong Decoction treats the above-mentioned conditions.

  • Ingredients:
    • 7 sheng of Mai Men Dong (Ophiopogon),
    • 1 sheng of Ban Xia (Pinellia),
    • 2 taels each of Ren Shen (Ginseng) and Gan Cao,
    • 3 heaping cups of Jing Mi (Glutinous Rice),
    • 12 large jujubes.

Boil these six ingredients in 12 sheng of water until 6 sheng remain. Take 1 sheng warm, three times during the day and once at night.

For the Sacred Victory Gold Tablets [from the "Jufang"], this treats acute closure of the throat, as well as conditions linked with single and double moths, tight throat, heavy tongue, and wooden tongue.

  • Ingredients:
    • Equal parts of Sulfur, Chuan Xiong (Szechuan Lovage), La Tea, Brain Mint, Chuan Wu (Black Aconite), Sheng Di Huang (Raw Rehmannia), and Niter, ground to a powder.

Mix with fresh green onion juice, dividing into ten tablets of 1 tael each. For use, take one tablet, first gargle with cool water, then chew 5-7 leaves of mint, and continue chewing the medicine with the mint before swallowing with well water. In severe cases, take three doses in succession.[109p]

Dan Huang San (Gall Powder)
For treating throat obstruction and swelling.
Half a qian of alum and two whole scorpions.
Grind these into a powder, use a chicken feather dipped in the medicine to place in the throat, and shortly after a sound will break forth; then use fresh lotus leaves ground finely, mixed with well water, and swallow; expelling toxic saliva will result in healing; if not expelled, take again.[110p]
Chicken Inner Gold Powder (Danxi)
Treats throat congestion, both single and double moth.

Dragon Brain Ointment (Jufang)
Treats throat phlegm, swelling, and pain.

Grind into powder, form honey pills the size of a marble, dissolve in the mouth and swallow.

Green Dragon Gall (Huoren)
Treats throat blockage and swelling, effective for both single and double moth.
Copper sulfate placed in the gall of a green fish, dried into powder, blown into the throat for immediate results. If there is no green fish, substitute with the gall of a carp. Best in the twelfth month.

Throat Blowing Powder (Gangmu)
Treats swollen and blocked throat.
Five qian of copper sulfate, if unavailable, substitute with green vitriol, put into the gall of a green fish, wind-dried; if no green fish, use the gall of a carp. Seven shelled snake beans, one qian of copper blue, two and a half qian of nitrate, ground separately. Five fen of light powder and one character of indigo. Mix the copper sulfate with the snake beans in a copper pan, remove the snake beans, combine with the other four ingredients, add a little musk. Use one character to blow into the throat, expectorate phlegm and blood, and recover immediately.[111p]
Qingliang San [from "Huichun", same below]
Treats real fire causing sore throat and swelling.

Jiawei Siwu Decoction

Longnao Podu San

Jinghuang Decoction (from "Into the Door"): Treats wind-heat stagnation, swollen and painful throat, and constipation. Ingredients: four qian of jingjie and one qian of dahuang. Chop the ingredients, boil in water, and take on an empty stomach.

Divine Efficacy Powder - Treats throat paralysis, causing voice loss.

Mix equal parts of Schizonepeta spikes and castor bean flesh into a powder. Form into honey-sized pills, wrap in cotton, and dissolve in the mouth.

Saliva-Removing Formula - Treats throat paralysis.

Use five qian of pig's tooth soapberry, one and a half qian of copper sulfate, five fen of indigo; grind into a powder. Mix with vinegar to form pills the size of cherries. Each pill should be wrapped in cooked silk and placed on the tip of a chopstick. Moisten with good vinegar, apply onto the throat ulcer. Bite the chopstick; if saliva flows like water, relief is achieved. Afterwards, take Fangfeng Tongsheng Powder.

Ice Plum Pills - Effective for eighteen types of throat paralysis; also treats throat wind swelling and pain remarkably.

Take thirty-five pieces of Tiannanxing, Banxia, white alum, white salt, Fangfeng, and nitrate rock (each four liang), two liang of Platycodon and one and seven-tenths liang of licorice (cooked), along with one hundred pieces of large plum fruits. Soak the nitrate in saltwater for a time, then crush all herbs, mix in water, and submerge the plum fruits in this mixture. The water level should cover the plums by three fingers. Soak for seven days, remove, and dry in the sun; then soak again, dry until the medicinal water is nearly gone. Finally, store the plums in a sealed ceramic jar; the frost-white coating is ideal. When using, wrap in cotton, hold in the mouth, and gradually swallow the juice; expectorate until recovery. An alternative recipe includes four liang of soapberry, without licorice.[117p]
Longnao Chuanxiong Pill: Treats various throat diseases, opening and benefiting the seven orifices, refreshing the spirit, clearing heat and resolving phlegm, eliminating wind and transforming stagnation. Ingredients: 5.3 taels of mint leaves, 1.5 taels of balloon flower root, 1 tael each of Chuanxiong, Fangfeng, and licorice, 0.5 taels of white cardamom, 0.3 taels of dried brain, 0.2 taels of sand ginger. Grind these ingredients into a powder, mix it with honey, and form into 20 pills for every 2 taels. Each pill should be chewed well and taken with clear tea, or dissolved in the mouth. This formula is similar to the decoction with added or subtracted mint.

Wuxiao Ointment: The throat reflects the condition of the spleen and stomach. If there is heat in the organs, the throat will become blocked, and the spirit energy will not flow freely; it is advisable to take this remedy. Ingredients: 10 taels of fresh Wuxiao, 3 taels of Cimicifuga, 2 taels each of antler horns, Tongcao, and peony root, 1 sheng of cut rose root, 5 sheng of sliced fresh Rehmannia, 2 jin of pig fat, and 6 zhu of mugwort leaves (fresh preferred). Grind these nine ingredients and wrap them in fine cloth, steep in 1 sheng of bitter wine overnight. Infuse into the pig fat over a low heat until the bitter wine evaporates and the ointment is quiet; strain out the dregs. The resulting ointment should be the size of a large almond, and should be slowly swallowed down the throat.

Another formula: For treating swollen painful throat wind and toxins impacting the heart and chest. Ingredients: 1.5 sheng of fermented soybeans, 2 taels each of rhinoceros horn, belamcanda, apricot kernels, and licorice, 3 taels of peony root, 7 pieces of gardenia, 4 taels of Cimicifuga, and 2.5 taels of antler horn. Grind these nine ingredients and decoct in 9 sheng of water until reduced to 3 sheng, then strain, add the fermented soybeans, and bring to a boil. Divide into three doses.[118p]
Wind Poison Formula: For treating wind poison when water cannot be swallowed.

Ingredients:

  • 6 taels of both Cimicifuga (Sheng Ma) and Peony (Shao Yao)
  • 3 taels each of Reed Rhizome (She Gan), Apricot Kernels (Xing Ren), Cypress gum (Feng Xiang), Kudzu Root (Ge Gen), and Ephedra (Ma Huang)
  • 2 taels of Licorice (Gan Cao)

Instructions:

  • Chew these eight ingredients and boil in eight liters of water until reduced to two and a half liters. Divide into three doses.

Mother Ginger Wine:
The throat indicates conditions of the liver and gallbladder. If there's internal heat, the throat will feel obstructed with closed breath. If there's internal cold, the throat will break and cause hoarseness. This remedy should be taken.

Ingredients:

  • 2 liters of Mother Ginger juice
  • 1 liter each of clarified butter, cow marrow, and oil
  • 1 tael each of Cinnamon (Gui Xin) and Qinjiao (Qin Jiao)
  • 1 and a half taels of Siler (Fang Feng)
  • 1 and 6/10 taels of Chuanxiong and Du Huo

Instructions:

  • Grind these nine ingredients into powder, add to ginger juice, boil gently with cow marrow and clarified butter for three cycles (up and down), then in the morning, warm 1 liter of clear wine, add 2 portions of the paste, and swallow carefully, three times a day and once at night.

Another Formula: For treating previous symptoms and throat pain with difficulty.

Ingredients:

  • 1 tael each of Danshen (Salvia), Sheng Ma, and powdered realgar (Xiong Huang)
  • 1 tael each of Apricot Kernels, Euphorbia (Gui Jiu), Licorice, and Reed Rhizome
  • Half a tael of Musk

Instructions:

  • Grind these eight ingredients into powder, make pills as big as Tongzi (a type of nut), take one pill with wine, increasing to five pills, three times a day.

Another Formula: For treating throat injury and unclear voice.

Ingredients:

  • 1 liter each of wine and clarified butter
  • 2 and a half taels of ground dried ginger
  • 2 taels each of Tong Cao, Cinnamon, and Acorus (Shi Chang Pu)

Instructions:

  • Mix these six ingredients and take a spoonful, three times a day.[119p]

Another recipe for treating throat discomfort and difficulty in breathing.

A decoction for treating mild throat obstruction.
Two qian each of raw rehmannia, peony, ophiopogon, and salvia; one qian of licorice; and one and a half qian of achyranthes. Boil with two sheng of water until reduced by a third and take warm on an empty stomach.

Two qian each of raw rehmannia, peony, and ophiopogon; three to five qian of cooked rehmannia; five to seven fen of honey-fried licorice; one qian each of anemarrhena and lycium peel. Boil with two sheng of water.

Si Yin Decoction - Treats cough and lung heat with throat obstruction.
Poria 1.5-2 grams, raw Rehmannia 2-3 grams, Ophiopogon 2 grams, Peony 2 grams, Lily bulb 2 grams, Adenophora 2 grams, raw Licorice 1 gram. Use 500 ml of water, decoct until reduced to 350 ml, and take away from meals.

Chou Xin Drink - Treats heat symptoms with throat obstruction.
Huangqin 1-2 grams, Dendrobium 1-2 grams, Mutong 1-2 grams, stir-fried Gardenia 1-2 grams, Huangbo 1-2 grams, Zhiqiao 0.5 grams, Zexie 0.5 grams, fine Licorice 0.3 grams. Xi Xin Drink - Treats throat obstruction with less severe heat.
Chenpi 0.8 grams, Huangqin 2 grams, Ophiopogon 1.5 grams, Peony 1.5 grams, Huangbo 1.5 grams, Poria 1.5 grams, and Moutan bark 1.5 grams. Use 500 ml of water, decoct until reduced to 350 ml, and take warm away from meals.

Lu Dou Drink - Treats various symptoms of throat heat obstruction.
Lu Dou (mung bean) in any amount, boil in ample water until mushy, add a pinch of salt or some honey, let cool; whether thick or thin, you may consume freely, up to three or four times a day as needed. This substance is not cold or bitter, does not harm spleen qi, is effective in detoxifying, alleviating annoyance, reducing heat, and quenching thirst, promoting urination, making it one of the best and easiest remedies. If there is intense heat and dry mouth, avoid rich flavors, just boil lightly, consume the clear broth cold, which is particularly effective for alleviating annoyance and clearing heat.[121p]
Snow Pear Decoction – for treating initial symptoms.
Peel a large, fragrant, and sweet pear, and place it in a large bowl filled with cold spring water. Thinly slice the pear and soak it in the water for a short while. The water will become sweet. Drink this water frequently, but do not consume the pear pulp, as it quickly counteracts excess yin fire.

Another method: Use one earthworm, grind it very finely, mix with egg white, and inject, which will relieve the blockage.

For throat swelling and blockage: Use a snail soaked in water, hold it in the mouth and swallow, which will work immediately. Another method: Take seven snails, two pieces of white plum flesh, grind them together, wrap in cotton, and hold in the throat for immediate effect.[139p]
Throat swelling and pain: Use lychee flowers and roots, boil them in water and sip the juice slowly, which will help in recovery. [From "Hai Shang Fang"]

A poem about throat issues: Severe throat swelling and obstruction are most concerning; quickly obtain oil from a large lamp. In serious cases, take only three or five sips; this remedy was left by a wise person.

Throat swelling and pain: Suck on chicken feces to get the juice in your throat. [From "Sheng Hui Fang"]

Throat swelling and pain: Take a piece of soapwort, peel it, soak it in rice vinegar, and roast it seven times without burning. Grind it to a powder, blow a little into the throat, and spitting saliva will result in recovery.

Throat swelling and wind: On the fifth of May or the sixth of June or the seventh of July, harvest paper mulberry leaves, dry them in the shade, and use one for powder; take it with well water. If severe, use two for recovery. [From "Ji Jian Fang"]

Throat ulcers: Layered and stacked, without pain, but after a long time, foul-smelling holes may appear, ruining appetite: use stinky tangerine leaves, boil them, and drink the decoction.

Severe throat wind: Use seven seeds of purgative bean; for raw ones, remove the shell and grind them; for cooked ones, remove the shell and burn them over a lamp, retaining the essence, and grind. Take two pieces of dried mulberry bark; one piece of realgar, finely grind; and one piece of turmeric, also grind. Combine these finely and take half a letter each time, adjusting with a little clear tea. If the mouth is locked and the throat is blocked, blow into the throat with a bamboo tube, and shortly after vomiting, relief will be attained. This is called the Realgar Powder.[140p]
Throat obstruction, speech cannot be emitted: use pig’s teeth soapberry and frost plum as powder to hold in the mouth.

Acupuncture

The "Suwen" states: When evil guests invade the channels of the hand's lesser yang, they cause throat obstruction, with a rolled tongue and dry mouth, heart distress, pain in the outer arm, and inability to lift the hand to the head. Needle the middle finger and the nail, withdrawing like chives, one puncture each, the strong will recover promptly, while the elderly may take a moment. Needle left for right, right for left. This is a new ailment, lasting several days. When evil guests invade the channels of the foot's lesser yin, they cause throat pain, with inability to eat, and inexplicable anger, causing qi to rush upward, needle the central pulse beneath the foot three punctures each, a total of six punctures, recovery is immediate. Needle left for right, right for left. If there is swelling in the throat preventing ingestion, and saliva cannot be expectorated, needle before the rhomboid bone, blood will flow and recovery is immediate. Needle left for right, right for left. If the lungs are deficient, there will be shortness of breath and inability to breathe deeply, with deafness and dry throat, target the channels of the greater yin's foot, the lesser sun's exterior, and the inner blood of the evil guest.

The "Ling Shu" states: The separate name of the foot's greater yang is Fenglong, when the qi counteracts, it will cause sudden throat obstruction and dumbness; it is advisable to use it. For blocked throat, target the zhaohai point.[141p]
Throat obstruction with a rolled tongue, dry mouth, troubled heart, heart pain, and internal arm pain that cannot reach the head; take the little finger under the nail, scraping it like chives. The throat is dry and the mouth hot like glue; take the foot's lesser yin. For throat obstruction that prevents speech, take the foot's yangming; if able to speak, take the hand's yangming. The "Hua Yi Classic" states: throat pain preventing speech is governed by the Tian Tu. For throat obstruction and chest rebellion, first take the Chong vessel, then the San Li and Yun Men, and drain them all. If the throat is swollen and speech is difficult, the Tian Zhu governs it.[142p]
Throat obstruction is governed by the points: Wan Gu, Tian Rong, Qi She, Tian Ding, Chi Ze, He Gu, Shang Yang, Yang Xi, Zhong Zhu, Qian Gu, Shang Qiu, Ran Gu, and Yang Jiao.

For throat obstruction with swelling and inability to swallow water or liquid, Xuan Ji governs it.

For throat obstruction with inability to swallow food, Jiu Wei governs it.

For throat obstruction with a sensation like a lump in the throat, San Jian governs it.

For throat obstruction with inability to speak, Wen Liu and Qu Chi govern it.

For throat obstruction with reversed qi, mouth deviation, and a sensation of constriction in the throat and pharynx, Xing Jian governs it.

For pain in the throat that prevents internal eating, Yong Quan governs it.

The “Qian Jin Fang” states: Feng Fu, Tian Kwang, and Lao Gong govern throat pain. Fu Tu, Tian Tu, and Tian Xi govern harsh voice and choking sensation in the throat. Shao Shang, Tai Chong, and Jing Qu govern sounds in the throat. Yu Ji governs dryness in the throat. Shui Tu governs swelling in the throat and pharynx. Ye Men and Si Du govern shortness of breath and pharyngeal lumps. Jian Si governs the sensation of a lump in the throat. Shao Chong governs sourness in the throat. Shao Fu and Li Gou govern the feeling of gas in the throat like a lump. Zhong Zhu, Zhi Gou, and Nei Ting govern throat pain. Fu Liu, Zhao Hai, Tai Chong, and Zhong Feng govern throat dryness. Qian Gu, Zhao Hai, and Zhong Feng govern asymmetrical swelling in the throat that makes swallowing difficult. Yong Quan and Da Zhong govern throat pain that prevents internal eating. Ran Gu and Tai Xi govern internal swelling in the throat, with the qi escaping to the throat, rendering one unable to speak.[143p]
Fengchi governs throat and pharynx disorders, leading to stiff neck and inability to bend. Wanggu, Tianyou, and Qiangu govern throat obstruction, swelling in neck and throat, with inability to look up or down, and cheek swelling extending to behind the ear. Zhongfu and Yangjiao govern throat obstruction along with fullness in the chest and symptoms of cold and heat. Tianrong, Quepen, Dazhu, Geyu, Yunmen, Chize, Erjian, Lidui, Yongquan, and Rangu govern throat obstruction and difficulty swallowing, with symptoms of cold and heat. Tianding, Qishe, and Geyu govern throat obstruction, leading to choking and swelling in the throat that cannot subside, making it difficult to swallow food and drink. Tiantu governs throat obstruction with a dry and urgent sensation in the throat. Daling and Pianli govern throat obstruction with a dry throat. Xuannv and Jiuyi govern throat obstruction with swelling in the throat, preventing liquid intake. Sanjian and Yangxi govern throat obstruction with feeling of choking in the throat. Shenmen, Hegu, and Fengchi govern throat obstruction. Sanli, Wenshu, Quchi, Zhongzhu, and Fenglong govern throat obstruction leading to inability to speak. Guanchong, Qiaoyin, and Shaoze govern throat obstruction, with a rolled tongue and dry mouth.[144p]
For throat obstruction and violent retching in the sides, first take the Chongmai, then the Sanli and Yunmen to drain. Additionally, puncture the tip of the little finger to draw blood, and it will take effect immediately. The "Eastern Garden Ten Books" states: for throat closure, puncture the Shaoyang Jing points on the hands and feet, namely Guanchong and Qiaoyin. In cases of throat closure with a milky moth, use the Shaoshang point, inserting the needle one depth and keeping it prone at a backward angle of three depth; also needle Zhaohai and Taichong. The "Danxi Heart Method" mentions that for throat closure, needle Shaoshang, Hegu, and Chize. For long-term throat obstruction, men treat the left side and women the right, applying moxibustion to the first segment of the thumb nail three times. The "Effective Recipe" states that if the throat remains closed, needling the Yangling point will result in immediate healing. For chronic throat issues, moxibustion should be applied seven times to a point half an inch below the earlobe and near the zygomatic bone, with two sets of seven being especially effective.[145p]
For sore throat and swelling, needle Fengfu, which is effective for all diseases of the throat and conditions such as toxic qi returning to the heart. Additionally, needle Shàoshāng, which treats sore and swollen throat. Furthermore, needle Hégǔ and Shàngxīng to treat swelling of the cheeks and wind affecting the throat. Also, needle Zú Sānlǐ.

The "Medical Essentials" states that the acupuncture methods for throat obstruction from the "Internal Canon" have two types: one based on the meridians passing through the throat and the other relating to other diseases that cause throat obstruction, encompassing the six meridians. The first involves the hand and foot Yangming meridians. It specifies that for throat obstruction preventing speech, one should needle the foot Yangming, and if speech is possible, needle the hand Yangming. It further states that the Stomach Meridian of the Foot Yangming runs from Dàyíng in front to Rénjīng, circling the throat; the resulting diseases include swelling in the neck and throat obstruction, requiring treatment based on the conditions of excess, deficiency, heat, and cold. Another mention is that the branch of the Foot Yangming, known as Fēnglóng, is located eight cun above the ankle, diverging to the Taiyin; if the pathogenic qi reverses, it leads to acute throat obstruction and muteness, requiring treatment at this branch point.[146p]
It is also said: The hand Yangming channel of the large intestine causes illnesses such as throat obstruction, from excessive heat or cold descending.

Secondly: For the hand Shaoyang, the classic states: The Sanjiao hand Shaoyang channel emerges above the clavicle, connecting behind the ear. When it is disturbed, it causes throat swelling and obstruction, from excessive heat or cold descending. It is further stated: When evil influences invade the hand Shaoyang collaterals, they cause throat obstruction. To treat this, needle the nails of the middle and index fingers, taking care to insert the needle as deep as a garlic leaf, with immediate effect in robust individuals, and delayed effect in the elderly. Treat the left side for the right side, and the right side for the left side.

Thirdly: The channels that pass through the throat are two. The classic states: The liver meridian of the foot Jueyin runs behind the throat, hence when there is pain behind the throat, this is the corresponding point. It also states: The kidney meridian of the foot Shaoyin traverses the diaphragm of the liver and runs along the throat.[147p]
What Dou Hanqing refers to as "必准" (must be accurate) pertains to addressing the blockage in the throat.

Fourthly: There is a condition where other diseases cause throat paralysis. The classic text states: When the heart coughs, the throat feels tight and obstructed, and in severe cases it leads to swelling and paralysis of the throat. To treat this, one should stimulate the heart's associated point, which is the Daling point.

For treating throat paralysis, use Fenglong, Yongquan, and Guanchong. In severe cases, utilize a small three-edged needle alongside a writing brush to simulate applying medication directly to the paralyzed throat, then puncture to release purple blood immediately for recovery.

For throat blockage, use Shaoshang, Yinbai, Shaochong, and Yongquan.

In cases of throat paralysis, if the jaw swells like a surge and water cannot be swallowed: stimulate the Shaoshang to cause bleeding; on the back of the big toe, at the last joint, apply three punctures with a three-edged needle to draw blood; and at Yanggu, puncture three times.

For throat paralysis, needle the Shaoyin point, located at the wrist along the artery behind the little finger. Insert the needle three times and supplement.

According to the Inner Canon, there are two moxibustion and acupuncture methods for throat swellings and pains. The first involves using the foot Shaoyin point.[148p]
The classic text states: The kidney channel corresponds to the lesser yin; the illnesses it causes are swelling of the throat, difficulty breathing, and pain in the throat. It also says: If there is swelling in the throat that cannot be ingested, and saliva cannot be expelled, one should puncture just before the bone to draw blood, which will immediately relieve the condition. Puncture the left side for the right side, and the right side for the left. Furthermore, it says: When evil energies affect the collateral of the lesser yin, it causes throat pain that makes it impossible to eat, anger without reason, and the upward flow of qi troubling the throat. Puncture centrally beneath the feet three times for a total of six punctures, which will immediately alleviate the condition. Puncture the left for the right, and the right for the left.

Secondly, one should access the hand taiyang. The classic states: The small intestine channel of the hand taiyang causes throat pain and swelling of the jaw if it is influenced by movement, which can be examined for its presence of deficiency or excess, cold or heat, and treated accordingly. The "Inner Canon" mentions moxibustion and puncturing the throat, specifically noting two techniques. The first technique involves accessing the Yanglingquan. It states: For those with gallbladder disease, who sigh frequently, experience a bitter mouth, vomit residual bile, and have a thick sensation in the throat resulting in frequent saliva secretion, one should access the Yanglingquan. This is the first technique. The second technique involves accessing the Daling.[149p]
The scriptures say: The condition of heart cough manifests as a throaty sensation, feeling like a blockage. This indicates the need to treat the heart's corresponding acupoint. The "Introduction to Medicine" states: When there is an accumulation of fire, one should induce bleeding through acupuncture, which is the same principle as sweating. The more blood is drawn, the better the recovery. For those with needle sores, ginger juice mixed with warm water should be sipped frequently. Generally, for blood blisters caused by tightness in the joints, it is most effective to use needles; for those not visible, have the patient hold water in their mouth and use a reed to prick the nostril to induce bleeding, which is quite effective.

The "Examination of Medical Formulas" mentions: In the case of acute throat obstruction, needle the area just outside the nail of the patient’s thumb, approximately the size of a chives leaf, with men on the left and women on the right—bleeding indicates effectiveness. If the situation is critical, needle both thumbs, which will yield prompt results. The throat is connected to the lungs, and the acupuncture point is Shaoshang, which is a lung aperture; hence, bleeding leads to recovery.

If the throat appears red and swollen, needle from the side to induce bleeding for recovery. It is essential to avoid piercing the Yamen point, as it could cause a loss of voice.[150p]
Guidance

The "Ancient and Modern Medical Collection" states: To treat throat obstruction, have the patient bend their thumb at the second joint and keep it curled, then open their mouth and bite firmly. This will facilitate the flow of qi, disperse the blood vessels, and the swelling will subside. The "Key Secrets of Preserving Life" suggests that for throat wind, one can push on the affected area to clear the lung meridian and then breathe in while blowing out.

Medical Case

The "Book of the Later Han" in Hua Tuo's biography states: Tuo once traveled and saw someone suffering from a blocked throat. He told them: "There used to be a pancake seller by the roadside whose pancakes were very sour; you can take three liters of his drink, and your ailment will surely disappear." Just as Tuo said, the patient immediately vomited a snake and then hung it on the cart to wait for Tuo. At that time, Tuo's young son was playing by the door and, seeing the situation, remarked to himself: "There must be something by the guest's cart; it must be my grandfather." When the guest approached and looked, he saw a snake hanging on the wall, and realized its peculiarity.[151p]
The "Rituals of Filial Piety" states: A woman fell ill with a swollen and obstructed throat, unable to swallow gruel or porridge. For several days, the swelling did not subside, and medicine was difficult to take while acupuncture was ineffective. A person suggested using angelica, schizonepeta, and licorice decocted in hot water for gargling, and cooling water to treat her hands. Within five or six days, the pain lessened and the swelling disappeared, allowing her to eat and drink as usual. Throat ailments are very urgent and should not be treated recklessly with needles or medicines.

The "Treasure Mirror of Health" mentions: A son of the Liang family, due to damage from excessive heat and dampness, suffered from overflowing heart fire affecting the lungs. Therefore, mulberry root and earth bone bark, which are slightly bitter and cool, were used to lower the internal fire in the lungs and replenish energy, serving as the chief remedy. Huangqin and Zhimu, both bitter and cold, were used to treat the foul, fishy breath and clear the lung qi, acting as the minister. To gather lung qi, it is urgent to consume sour foods; the sourness of Schisandra helps gather lung qi, while Mai Men Dong is sweet, bitter, and cool, treating thick, sticky phlegm and dryness in the mouth and tongue, serving as an assistant. Platycodon, light, acrid, and warm, treats phlegm reversal and benefits the throat, serving as a messager. In the spring of the Wucheng year, many in the village suffered from throat paralysis, likely due to the invasion of the qi at the end of the previous year and the beginning of this year, which brought about the dual fire evils. A sweet orange decoction was used, adding Huangqin, Lian, Banxia, Jangcan, Shucanzizi, and Pueraria to dispel it. For those who were weak, ginseng, astragalus, and angelica were added. When water and gruel could not enter, a detoxifying wax gourd pill was first used, administered as a liquid; after phlegm was expelled, ginger juice was given. None who took the previous medicine failed to see remarkable results. However, if cold, sour substances were used excessively, they would be ineffective, as the evil would be trapped and unable to be released.[152p]
"The Miraculous Remedies" states: Yang Lizhi, returning to Chuzhou from his post in Guangfu, developed an abscess in his throat, which grew swollen and then burst, causing pus and blood to flow continuously both day and night. He could neither eat nor sleep, and the physicians were at a loss for how to treat him. Coincidentally, Elder Yang Ji was summoned by the governor, and Lizhi's two sons hurriedly went to invite him. Upon arriving, he looked carefully for a long time and said, “There is no need to take the pulse; I already know what it is. However, this illness is quite peculiar; you must first consume one pound of fresh ginger slices before any medication can be administered. Otherwise, there is no other way.” After saying this, he left. The sons had difficulty accepting this advice and said, “How can we eat fresh ginger when there is pus and pain in the throat?” Lizhi replied, “Elder Ji’s medical knowledge is profound, and his words are not in vain; try taking a slice and see if you can swallow it. If not, then it won’t cause harm to stop altogether.” They then consumed the ginger, finding it surprisingly sweet and fragrant. They gradually increased the amount to about half a pound, and the pain began to ease. Once they consumed a full pound, they finally felt a spicy taste, and the pus and blood ceased immediately. They could drink congee without any obstruction. The next day, they invited Elder Ji to thank him and inquire further. He responded, “You live in the south and often eat partridges. This bird likes to eat pinellia, which can be toxic over time, hence the use of ginger to counter it. Now that the source of the illness has been cleared, there is no need for other medications.” One son recalled that in a Tang dynasty novel, it was recorded that Duke Cui Wei suffered from a similar ailment, and a physician named Liang Xin diagnosed it as food poisoning. When asked what he had eaten, he said he often enjoyed bamboo chicken, which tends to eat pinellia sprouts, and this was likely the source of the toxin. The physician then ordered ginger juice to be mixed and administered to him, resulting in recovery. This case is indeed similar to that.[153p]
The "Medical Essentials" states: Sun Yapban treated Pan Yuan, who was choking. Sun used half a coin's worth of medicine and blew it into his throat. After a moment, Pan coughed up pus and blood and was immediately healed. Pan visited Sun to express his gratitude, saying: "This was a matter of great urgency, and without your esteemed self, I could not have been saved. In urgent situations, it is not medicine that can heal but a skilled hand." He offered a reward of one hundred taels of silver and requested the formula to help with emergencies. Sun replied: "Use equal parts of pig's tooth, soapwort, and alum, place them on a new tile, and roast them dry to make a powder." After giving him the formula, he did not accept the offered reward.[154p]
"The Medical Case Records of Xue Ji" states:

Tong Fu Li Chao experienced sore throat and mouth sores. This was due to wind-heat in the upper jiao. He first used two doses of Jing Fang Bai Du, and his throat pain gradually improved; then with the use of Yuan Shen Sheng Ma Decoction, his mouth and tongue healed completely.

Di Guan Huang Bei had a sore throat, excessive thirst, and constipation. This indicated heat in both the upper and lower regions. He was treated with Fang Feng Tong Sheng Powder and recovered quickly.

A man had a swollen sore throat, and I wanted to use acupuncture to release the poison; however, he feared needles and only took medicine. Eventually, he could not swallow even cooked food. I quickly performed acupuncture at the affected area to draw out toxic blood and then gave him a cleansing medicine for the throat, leading to recovery.

Di Guan Hu Cheng Fu had a dry throat and pain, indicating deficiency-heat in the kidney and bladder pathways. I used Si Wu Decoction with additions of Huang Lian, Zhi Mu, and Yuan Shen. After four doses, he had slight improvement; then, with one dose of Ren Shen Gu Ben Pill, he did not relapse.

Zhi Fang Lu Yi Zhai had a swollen sore throat, blurry vision, and reddish, cloudy urine. This indicated damp-heat in the bladder. He was treated with Si Ling Powder plus Huang Lian, Zhi Mu, Yin Chen, and Fang Ji, and recovered quickly; later he also took Liu Wei Di Huang Wan to fully heal.[155p]
A Confucian scholar, Wang Wenyuan, had a sore throat and ulcers in his mouth, which worsened with exertion. I diagnosed a deficiency in spleen and lung qi, with heat in the bladder. I prescribed a formula to tonify the middle and benefit qi, adding codonopsis, pan-roasted black phellodendron, and anemarrhena; upon slight improvement, I removed the phellodendron and anemarrhena, adding shan zhu and yam, resulting in complete recovery.

Another scholar, over fifty years old, experienced throat pain. Taking cooling medicine or overexertion exacerbated the pain, indicating deficiency of middle qi and heat. I prescribed a formula to tonify the middle and benefit qi, adding pan-roasted black scutellaria and bulbus, and he recovered after four doses; I then removed the scutellaria and bulbus, and after several more doses, he fully healed.

A scholarly gentleman found that when his feet felt hot, his throat would start to hurt, accompanied by internal heat, dry mouth, and phlegm rising. This indicated kidney deficiency with excess heat. I prescribed a formula to tonify the middle and benefit qi, adding wheat husk and five-flavor fruit, using a modified Eight Flavor Pill, which led to complete recovery.

An elderly man suffered from a sore throat and frequent, red urination, which worsened in the afternoon. This was indicative of bladder yin deficiency. I aimed to nourish the source, using a formula to tonify the middle and benefit qi, adding pan-roasted black phellodendron and anemarrhena. After four doses, his throat pain improved; I then removed the two components and added shan zhu, yam, wheat husk, and five-flavor fruit, resulting in immediate recovery.

A gentleman had throat swelling and was unable to swallow medication. Acupuncture at the painful area caused purple blood to emerge, and he felt slightly better. Using Po Guandan to dissolve, I then prescribed a clear throat and promote diaphragm formula, leading to prompt recovery.

A gentleman who regularly drank alcohol experienced throat pain, internal heat with thirst, and difficulty urinating, while his appetite remained normal. This indicated accumulated heat in the bladder. I prescribed a formula based on the Four Ling Decoction, adding yin chen and rhubarb. After four doses, his symptoms gradually receded, and I then provided a heart-clearing lotus seed drink for his comfort.[156p]
A certain astrological scholar, exhausted and entering a room, felt his throat tightening with pain, phlegm rising, and his limbs suddenly becoming hot. This indicated a deficiency of yin with the upward excitement of yang. I prescribed a decoction of Ba-zhen Tang (Supplement the Middle and Benefit Qi Decoction) with the addition of Fu Zi, and he recovered.

In the winter of the Gui-Mao year, the Vice Minister Jiang Shichuan consulted me. His pulse was floating and slightly strong at the right inch, and he had sores in his mouth. I said, "This is stomach fire affecting the lungs. You should have a light diet and be careful with your daily activities." In the autumn of the Jia-Chen year, he consulted me again, and his pulse at the chi position was flooding and rapid yet without strength. I said, "This indicates that the lung metal cannot generate kidney water; you need to rest to nourish the source of transformation." He complained of dryness and pain in his throat and ears, and his limbs occasionally felt hot, saying that if there were a fire without root, his demise was certain. Later, he mentioned to Liu Guxia that Lizhai suspected his illness was doubtful.

Come the spring of the Yi-Si year, Guxia told me, "Mr. Jiang's condition has already reached the critical point." We went to see him together, and indeed, his throat was swollen and ulcerated, with a more pronounced pulse. Some tried using hot herbs, which hastened his passing.

In another case, Wu Shangshe, over fifty years old, suffered from swollen and painful throat. Sometimes blood would be drawn with acupuncture. Though his mind was clear, his chi pulse was flooding and rapid, yet there was no regularity, and upon pressing it was weak as though nonexistent. I remarked, "Though there is form, there is no pain; this is a manifestation of yang. You must supply the yin robustly. If you instead damage the yin blood, you will certainly die." Eventually, he did pass away. This condition was caused by kidney qi deficiency, with rootless fire flaring upwards. Only through the modified Bawei Pill could one hope to return the fire to its source and perhaps save him.[157p]
Within the cloud bridge of the government academy, there was a case of postnatal throat pain, and taking heat-clearing medications only worsened the condition. Upon examination, I determined it was due to a deficiency in the urinary bladder meridian. The pulse of the bladder ascends, reaching the neck and returning. I administered Ba Zhen Decoction, along with peony root, Chai Hu, and toasted black and yellow berberine, leading to recovery.

In another case, Shen Da Fang had occasional phlegm in the throat, which prompted him to look left and spit it out, resulting in neck pain so intense that he could not turn his head. By night, the symptoms worsened, including night sweats and cold, numb hands and feet. He required assistance to get up or lie down, and any movement caused pain radiating to the heart and abdomen, creating countless degrees of suffering for three to four days. When I examined him, I said: this is the result of anger provoking liver fire, causing the gallbladder to generate heat and the tendons to contract. I prescribed Liu Wei Di Huang Wan with added gardenia and Chai Hu to clear the liver fire and nourish gallbladder blood. Within a day, his laughter and movements returned to normal, and when he met with guests, they did not recognize him as the same person who had been ill just days before.

A woman suffered from throat pain that ulcerated after two months, followed by generalized pain in her muscles and bones. I suspected it was a case of Yangmei sore poison, so I first treated her with several doses of Bi Xie Decoction, which alleviated her condition. I then prescribed over twenty doses of Si Wu Decoction combined with Bi Xie and astragalus, leading to the resolution of all her symptoms.[158p]
A child suffering from a mouth ailment for over a year, which spread to the whole body, was treated with powdered rhizoma of dioscorea mixed with milk. The mother also used boiled water for administration, and after a month, the child recovered.

A man initially suffered from a sore throat, followed by the appearance of various sores that were treated with light powders, but the condition recurred. After taking the previous medications again, the sores worsened, leading to severe ulceration of the hard palate, connecting with the nasal cavity. He had several lumps the size of peaches on his arms and wrists, which did not heal for over a year, showing evident signs of deficiency. I prescribed a treatment primarily with powdered rhizoma of dioscorea, along with remedies to strengthen the spleen, and he was stable after a month.

According to "Qidong Yeyu": the illness of throat closure is rapid and severe. It has been passed down by predecessors to use only one ingredient, alum, but sometimes it does not always prove effective. In the year of Xinchou, while I was attending to my parent and returning from Fujian, I encountered many cases of this ailment on the way, with one family of more than ten people succumbing in a single night. The roads were silent, and travelers were fearful. Upon reaching Nanpu, an old doctor advised using duckbill胆矾 (alum) finely ground and mixed with strong vinegar for administration, which gave us courage on the way back, though we still did not know its ultimate efficacy.

One day, while my first son was supervising by the riverside, an old soldier who had been careful came to me in tears, asking for help, saying his elderly wife had suffered from severe throat closure for three days and was on the brink of death. I happened to have a small amount of medicine in my medicine chest, so I gave it to him and instructed him to use it as directed. The next day, he joyfully bowed in the courtyard, saying: "As soon as she swallowed the medicine, she vomited profusely, releasing several pounds of phlegm, and she was cured." After that, whenever I treated several others, all showed immediate evidence of recovery. However, genuine alum is hard to find; those dedicated to health should not neglect to stock it for future use.[159p]
Court physician Zhang Ruhuan suffered from a severe sore throat as the day progressed, arising from a deficiency of qi and blood combined with heat. He was treated with the Eight Treasure Decoction and recovered. Later, whenever he entered a room, he experienced fever and headaches. He was prescribed a strengthening formula, supplemented with wheat husk, five-flavor herb, and Six Flavor Pill for regular use, after which he no longer experienced these issues.

Autumn official Ye Ren'an, whose constitution was primarily Yin deficient, suffered sudden throat swelling and alternating cold and heat due to anger, along with headaches, neck stiffness, and involuntary urination—the signs of liver fire. The liver governs sinews and the fiery condition caused swelling; excessive fire leads to blood depletion and muscle spasms, and overactivity of the liver resulted in urgent eye strain and neck tension, as well as weakness in the bladder causing involuntary urination. Thus, he was treated by needling the affected area to release toxic blood, and given prescriptions including Four Substances, Bupleurum, Gardenia, Scrophularia, and Licorice, leading to recovery. Additionally, he was given the Six Flavor Pill to nourish liver blood and replenish kidney water, resolving all symptoms.[160p]
The magistrate Ye Tianpei had a swollen and painful throat, with phlegm not being expelled, hot hands and feet, and a preference for cold food and drinks. He was treated with two doses of Qing Yan Li Ge Decoction, but there was no response; acupuncture at the Shaoshang point and Hou Shaokuan point resulted in phlegm exiting through the nose like glue, and purple blood coming from the affected area. After a week, he coughed out foul pus and recovered.

A Confucian scholar, after attending three lectures, suddenly had a swollen throat that obstructed his ability to speak, losing consciousness, with difficulty breathing and an influx of phlegm, sweating profusely, and experiencing weakness in his limbs. His pulse was floating, large, and rapid. This was due to overexertion and a rootless virtual fire flaring up. He was treated with a dose of Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction with added cinnamon, which immediately revived him.

The righteous man Gu Keming experienced throat pain, which developed into a fever at night. This was due to excessive liver fire with a deficiency in yin. He was treated with Si Wu Decoction combined with fried black Coptis,zhi mu, wheat ears, and five flavors, leading to his recovery. Later, due to overexertion, his throat swelled and closed up again. Acupuncture in the affected area caused bleeding; he was treated with Jie Geng Decoction to expel phlegm, leading to improvement. During mid-summer, he had a dry cough, hoarseness, thirst, and fever, with hot feet in the afternoon. Using Zi Shen Wan and Jia Jian Ba Wei Wan, he intermittently took them for over three months, and was pleased to find his health restored.

A woman had a swollen and painful throat, accompanied by constipation. She was treated with one dose of Feng Yin Tong Sheng Powder, and all her symptoms receded. Following that, she took three doses of Jing Feng Bai Du Powder and was stable. For this condition, if it is mild, treat with Jing Feng Bai Du Powder or Chui Hou Powder; if more severe, the best effect comes from using a Golden Key along with bleeding at the affected area. Otherwise, it may not help. Acupuncture at the Shaoshang points is also effective, but it is not as rapid as directly treating the affected area.[161p]
A man suffered from sore throat and swelling, with a rapid and full pulse. After administering a dose of Liangge San, the pain stopped. When combined with Jingfang Baidu San and added to Baipenzi in two doses, the swelling and pain subsided. Then, with another two doses of Jingfang Baidu San, and four doses of licorice, balloon flower, schizonepeta, saposhnikovia, and yuanshen, he regained stability.

A man had a swollen and obstructed throat, with excessive phlegm. After applying alum in the throat, he coughed up a bowl of phlegm. He then took Qingyan Lige Tang in four doses and felt at ease.

A man experienced pain in his throat, unable to swallow medication. After acupuncture at the affected area released a small amount of purple blood, he melted Po Guandan in his mouth, followed by taking Qingyan Xiaodu San, and he recovered.

A man suffered from dryness and pain in the throat. Administering a modified Siwu Decoction with Huanglian, Zhimu, and Yuanshen in four doses led to slight improvement. After taking Renshen Gudan Wan in one dose, he did not relapse.

A man had throat pain that worsened in the afternoon, with a rapid but weak pulse. A modified Siwu Decoction with Huanglian, Zhimu, Jing, and Fang was given in four doses, leading to recovery. The previous formula was adjusted to remove Jing and Fang, adding Yuanshen, licorice, and balloon flower; after several doses, he did not experience any further issues.

A court official from Putian suffered from throat closure, treated with Fangfeng Tongsheng San, but he could not swallow due to swelling. I suggested acupuncture was necessary, but his jaws were clenched. Therefore, I pierced the Shaoshang point, which drew blood, and his mouth opened immediately. I then applied alum to the affected area, resulting in the expulsion of about two bowls of phlegm, and he then recovered with the previous medication. I have often seen patients with this affliction, who fear needles and avoid acupuncture, often lead to death.[162p]
An old man experienced a sore throat, which was particularly severe in the afternoon. He was cured by taking a decoction of Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang with a few pieces of pan-fried Huang Bo and Zhi Mu.

A man had painful swollen breasts, with a floating and rapid pulse, but no pus had formed yet. After needling to release bad blood, he took two doses of Jing Fang Bai Du San and the swelling resolved.

Another man also had painful swollen breasts and was unable to eat. The ulcer was white, and pus had formed. After needling, the pus came out, and he felt better.

A man experienced swelling and pain in the throat, with a pulse that was initially floating and rapid, then became deeper and more solid. After taking one dose of Fang Feng Tong Sheng San, he had a bowel movement, and the condition quickly improved. Following this, he took two doses of Jing Fang Bai Du San and the swelling disappeared.

One patient was almost breathless, but his heart was still warm. He urgently needled the affected area, and black blood was released, leading to his revival. Both Bao Fu Qing and Qiao Shi Yu had experienced this condition, and they were cured by needling to draw out the blood. Generally, throat conditions are caused by fire, which can be very harmful and act swiftly. It’s crucial to determine the urgency and whether pus has formed.

If there is swelling and blockage, death could occur in an instant; it's advisable to use a golden key to clear the affected area, expel phlegm and saliva, allowing air to flow freely. If, after expelling, it is still closed, then it is due to bad blood or toxic pus, and urgent needling is necessary; otherwise, it may not be treatable.

The ancients said: treating the fire causing throat blockage is akin to extinguishing a fire; there is no time to delay. Additionally, it’s said: “Ride a horse and inspect the throat closure.” Indeed! There are many methods for treating the throat, but only needling has the power to restore life. Even without needling, simply using the juice of Wan Nian Qing in the throat and expelling it can lead to recovery.[163p]
A man experienced pain in his throat, with phlegm causing a blockage. I intended to treat him with Jingfang Baidu San, adding Lianqiao, Shanzhizi, Yuanshen, and Niubangzi. However, he had taken cool,甘寒 (sweet and cool) medicines to降火 (reduce fire), which instead intensified his fever and the swelling in his throat worsened. In an urgent move, I needled the Shaoshang points and continued with the previous medicine, adding Ma Huang to induce sweating, and all symptoms gradually subsided. Only a purple area in the throat remained painful, indicating it might lead to pus; thus, I removed Ma Huang from the previous medicine for one dosage, and once the pus discharged, he recovered.

For throat pain, if treated early or in mild cases, it is advisable to use Jingfang Baidu San to disperse it. If treatment is delayed or in severe cases, needling Shaoshang points is necessary. If blood stasis has formed, it must be needled at the affected area, and needling Shaoshang is also applicable. If the throat is still uncomfortable but not entirely resolved, it will surely lead to pus; however, once the pus is eliminated, recovery follows. If there is constipation, even after needling to release blood, one must use Fangfeng Tongsheng San to promote movement. Sweet and cool medicines should not be used unless there is true heat.[164p]
In the case of a county magistrate suffering from a swollen and painful throat, with chills and fever, and a rapid pulse, it was determined that the illness stemmed from the interplay of the lesser yin heart fire and the lesser yang fire channels. This condition was particularly severe, and the best treatment was to bleed the affected area. However, he was fearful of needles, so I first treated him with a cooling decoction. The medicine emerged from his nose; in haste to perform acupuncture, his jaw had already stiffened, making it impossible to needle. Thus, I needled the two points at the lesser commerce, manually pressed out the black blood, and his mouth opened immediately. I then needled between his throat and treated it with the previous medicine and a gold key to blow the area, leading to instant relief. Additionally, I prescribed a decoction of ginseng and a detoxifying powder with the addition of scutellaria, coptis, and arnebia seeds. After four dosages, he stabilized. The classical text states: "When fire is trapped, induce sweating or bleeding; it is one aspect of inducing sweat." The Hejian record states: "The fire causing throat closure must be treated with the same urgency as rescuing a fire, with no negligence allowed." It is common to encounter cases where throat closure does not yield to bleeding, or throat wind persists without clearing phlegm, resulting in many being beyond help. For each case of throat swelling and pain, or ulceration and toxicity, I have successfully used a decoction of schizopeplus and detoxifying powder with the addition of scutellaria and coptis; for more severe cases, I prescribed a wind-dispersing detoxifying powder, which proved effective.

A Mr. Du experienced swelling and pain in the throat, with lesions on his tongue, and was initially treated with a cooling throat and detoxifying powder in two doses, followed by a ginseng and peony decoction, resulting in recovery.

A man in his thirties frequently suffered from ulcerations in his mouth and tongue, appearing as if lacking skin, or having throat-related conditions. After taking a cooling throat and stomach-purging powder, his symptoms worsened, so I treated him with a regulating middle decoction, leading to recovery.[165p]
Wang Wenyuan had a swollen throat and mouth sores, worsening with fatigue. He was treated with a modified Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang, adding Yuan Shen, wine-fried Zhi Mu, and Huang Lian, and he recovered.

A man experienced throat pain with a rapid pulse. He was treated with Jing Fang Bai Du San, adding Qiang Huo and Lian Qiao for two doses, which improved slightly. After removing Qiang Huo and Lian Qiao, he received another two doses and recovered.

A man had a swollen and closed throat, with a tightly clenched jaw, preventing needles from penetrating. First, he was needled at the Shaoshang points, resulting in black blood discharge. His mouth immediately opened, allowing further needling at the affected area, and after taking a dose of Qing Yan Li Ge San, he recovered.

The "Medical Essentials" states: One day, Lord Wenlu had a swollen throat, and the Hanlin throat expert treated him. After three days, the condition worsened, and the Emperor appointed Sun to treat him. Sun said: "If I had a pen tube from Your Excellency, I could use it to apply medicine directly to the throat, and your condition would improve." Sun hurried to prick the throat; the Lord fainted, causing panic among those present. Sun then laughed, saying, "It is not that I cannot save him." In a moment, he vomited out purulent blood and, after ten days, returned to normal. The Emperor was pleased and praised Sun as an excellent doctor with remarkable skills.

I once treated a man with throat blockage by needling the Tai Xi point, causing half a cup of black blood to discharge, leading to recovery. Thus, it is said that throat blockage results from stagnant toxic blood. In treating this condition, one must first disperse the stagnant blood; if dispersing is ineffective, then phlegm should be addressed; if phlegm does not improve the condition, then the toxic blood must be expelled.[166p]
"Ancient and Modern Medical Systems" states: A man brought two servants into the capital, and one of them suddenly suffered from throat wind, swelling and blocking the airway, on the verge of death. He inquired of the local people and learned that there was a family of physicians named Li who specialized in throat ailments, so he ordered his servant to seek their help. Li Hai said: The condition is very dangerous; fortunately, you came here; otherwise, there would be no doubt of death. He then took a piece of paper from a box, rolled it, ignited it, and when the smoke rose, he quickly blew it out, instructing the servant to open his mouth and pierce the throat. Soon, the servant coughed out half a cup of purple blood, and at that moment, his breathing eased, allowing him to speak and eat porridge. After administering a powdery medicine, he was cured immediately. The man admired his remedy and secretly inquired about his secret; it was because he had previously coated the paper with dadura oil, so it ignited upon use, delivering its poisonous gas directly to the ailment.

Another person suffered from throat swelling and pain, unable to eat, with a fever and headache, and constipation. The opinions of the many doctors were conflicting; they all believed the heat required cooling medicine. A skilled physician said: The tight and rapid pulse is due to cold. The many doctors disagreed. The skilled physician said: I have a method to test for cold and heat. In the room, he lit a fire and used a decoction of scallions to steam the patient. If it were a heat illness, warm conditions would surely cause sweating, but if it were a cold, there would be no sweat, even with the bath. The patient trusted his words and bathed without sweating. In the bathing room, he took a dose of ephedra decoction; after a short while, he broke into a profuse sweat, his bowels moved, and he was well again. The other doctors admired his skill. Generally, discerning heat illness from cold using this method is most excellent.[167p]
The "Medical Formulation Examination" states: The "Record of Famous Physicians" mentions that when Princess Li Wang suffered from a throat abscess, her pain and swelling lasted for several days, and she could not eat or drink. When the medical officials were summoned, they all advised that she must use acupuncture and incision. The princess, upon hearing of needles and knives, cried and refused treatment. Due to the pain and inability to ingest water or food, a country doctor said: "I won't use any knives or needles; I will only dip a fine point of a brush in medicine and apply it to the abscess, and it will burst forth immediately." The princess was pleased and ordered him to be called. After applying the medicine twice, pus and blood spilled out more than a cup, and she felt relief. After two days, the sore showed no issues, and she instructed that his method be provided. The doctor explained: "I simply tied a needle to the brush tip and gently scraped until it burst; there is no other method."

The "Orthodox Surgery" states: A man had a swollen and painful throat, felt cold and fatigued, and his pulse was thin and strong. This indicated an exterior condition. A formula of Jingfang Baidu San was used, adding Burdock and Scrophularia, and the exterior symptoms retreated, but the swelling and pain remained. Another two doses of Scrophularia Detoxifying Decoction were administered, reducing the swelling and pain by half; after two more doses, he became stable.

Another man had a swollen and painful throat, with excessive phlegm. A gold key was used to first expel the thick phlegm, and Qingyan Lihge Decoction was employed to clear the accumulated heat. The swelling and pain slightly reduced, but it remained very red, indicating heat. Two doses of Huanglian Jiedu Decoction were given, with added Platycodon, and both the redness and swelling receded, leading to stability.[168p]
A man who frequently drank strong liquor suddenly found his throat swollen and blocked, unable to speak with a stiff tongue and obstructed phlegm, putting him in a perilous condition. He first used a needle to prick the Shaoshang acupoint; his mouth was able to open. Then, he used tung oil and chicken feathers to expel thick phlegm, bringing up several bowls’ worth before his voice returned. He also used a needle on the swelling, which drew out purple blood, then rinsed with warm water and applied ice borax powder. He added Liangge San with Glauber’s salt and Tianhuafen to alleviate the accumulated heat, and finally prescribed two doses of Lianqiao San for stabilization.

A woman had a slightly swollen throat with a pale complexion, struggling to swallow. Upon examining her pulse, it was also faint and weak, indicating a deficiency in middle Qi and false heat. She was given two doses of Lizhong Decoction, which immediately relieved her pain; then, she took Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction with pan fried Huangbo and Zhi Mu several times, and she did not experience a recurrence.

Another woman was very stout, suffering from a swollen and painful throat due to summer heat, with upper phlegm obstruction preventing her from speaking, putting her in a serious state. First, she used a needle to draw out toxic blood; then, with a golden key, she expelled thick phlegm in five or six bowls, after which a dose of Qingyan Lige Decoction slightly reduced the swelling and pain. After removing the salt and sulfide, she took more medication and stabilized.

A man was very fatigued, with a swollen and painful throat. He tried taking a throat-soothing decoction without effect. Upon examination, his pulse was thin and weak, indicating a deficiency due to overwork and false heat. In the morning, he took Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction with Mai Dong, Wu Wei Zi, Jie Geng, and Yuan Shen, and in the evening, he took Si Wu Decoction with Huangbo, Zhi Mu (fried black), and Gan Jiang, adding child's urine with the doses. Within a few days, the swelling and pain disappeared, and his fatigue alleviated, restoring his throat.[169p]
A man suffered from increasing swelling and pain. He took throat-clearing and digestive medicines, but they did not help. He was determined to produce pus. To counteract this, I administered the Feng Tong Sheng San, reducing the use of both nitrate and yellow medicine. His throat was swollen and painful, but after acupuncture, he was cured.

In the "Complete Works of Jingyue," it says: A friend of mine, Wang Pengque, was in his thirties and initially unrecognizable. He had a throat affliction for more than ten days. Upon my examination, I saw that his face and head were swollen, his throat and neck were extremely thick, he breathed heavily and his voice was hoarse, with swelling and mouth sores, causing him intense pain. A servant had been unable to lie down for several days. Upon checking his pulse, it was very thin and weak; when he spoke, his voice was faint. Inquiring about the medicines he had taken, they were all related to herbs like Scutellaria, Coptis, Gardenia, and Rhubarb. This was likely due to damage to the Yin, compounded by the invasion of cold, leading to excess cold at the lower part and blocking Yang at the top. Consequently, water and drink could hardly enter, and he was particularly fearful of heat. I said: "This is serious! If we delay half a day more, it will be too late for treatment." So I prepared a cooling Yin decoction with cold water and let him drink it slowly. After consuming one decoction, he had a swollen and painful head and neck, but all symptoms disappeared by morning.

The next day, when I saw him again, he had lost weight and looked emaciated, unlike his previous bloated self. I then continued treatment with several doses of the Five Blessings drink and he gradually recovered. Those who doubted were initially shocked, but later, they were grateful to me for bringing him back from the brink, resulting in a deep bond of friendship.[170p]
A woman in her thirties came to my home, suffering from exhaustion and pain in her throat due to a sore. She had seen many doctors without success. Upon examining her pulse, I found it rapid and weak; her symptoms indicated frequent loose stools. While asking about the treatments she had tried, she mentioned that they all involved clearing heat and removing fire. However, the more they cleared the fire, the worse her throat pain became. Upon careful observation, I realized that her issue was not due to excess heat and that she had been using too many cold and cooling remedies, which led to an empty feeling in her abdomen. Thus, I decided to specifically use nourishing herbal formulas like the Yin Replenishing Decoction and the Great Tonifying Yuan Decoction. In less than half a month, her throat pain reduced, and in less than six months, she was completely cured.[171p]
